\section{Entry-Level One-Line Classification Theorem for the Jacobian Remainder}

\section{Short explanation}

Once the full local residual Jacobian
\[
J_f=DG(\delta_f)
\]
is extracted, the only remaining matrix uncertainty is
\[
\boxed{
R_f:=J_f-J_f^{(4)}.
}
\]

The correct next branch is determined entirely by the matrix type of \(R_f\).
This section rewrites the previously abstract diagnostics
\[
\alpha_f,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm diag},\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm sym},\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}
\]
directly in terms of the entries of \(R_f\), so that the next step can be decided by one line of norm calculations.

\section{1. Exact baseline data}

The corrected branch is frozen at
\[
\delta_f=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096),
\qquad
\|G(\delta_f)\|\approx 0.03791852545979427,
\]
and the quartic baseline Jacobian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_f^{(4)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
10.095240102467715 & -4.991665534361308 & 0.41377801570768584\\
-4.991665534361308 & 22.64650843997611 & -1.2413340471230576\\
0.41377801570768584 & -1.2413340471230576 & 3.6033950146440785
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

Its smallest eigenvalue is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_*:=\lambda_{\min}(J_f^{(4)})\approx 3.5212959.
}
\end{equation}

So for the extracted full Jacobian \(J_f\), the quartic-relative size parameter is
\[
\alpha_f=\|R_f\|_2/\lambda_*.
\]

\section{2. Direct entry formulas in the coarse \((A,E,O)\) basis}

Write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_f=
\begin{pmatrix}
r_{11}&r_{12}&r_{13}\\
r_{21}&r_{22}&r_{23}\\
r_{31}&r_{32}&r_{33}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

Define the total Frobenius energy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_f:=\|R_f\|_F^2
=
r_{11}^2+r_{22}^2+r_{33}^2
+
r_{12}^2+r_{13}^2+r_{21}^2+r_{23}^2+r_{31}^2+r_{32}^2.
}
\end{equation}

Then the diagonal fit defect is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}^2
=
\frac{
r_{12}^2+r_{13}^2+r_{21}^2+r_{23}^2+r_{31}^2+r_{32}^2
}{
S_f
}.
}
\label{eq:epsdiag_entry}
\end{equation}

So \(\varepsilon_{\rm diag}\) is exactly the square root of the off-diagonal energy fraction.

Next, the best symmetric approximation is
\[
\frac12(R_f+R_f^T),
\]
hence the symmetric-fit defect is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}^2
=
\frac{
(r_{12}-r_{21})^2+(r_{13}-r_{31})^2+(r_{23}-r_{32})^2
}{
2S_f
}.
}
\label{eq:epssym_entry}
\end{equation}

This is exactly the skew-energy fraction.

Likewise, the pure symmetric off-diagonal fraction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm off}^2
=
\frac{
(r_{12}+r_{21})^2+(r_{13}+r_{31})^2+(r_{23}+r_{32})^2
}{
2S_f
}.
}
\label{eq:epsoff_entry}
\end{equation}

The diagonal energy fraction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm D}^2
=
\frac{r_{11}^2+r_{22}^2+r_{33}^2}{S_f}.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact identity is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
1=\varepsilon_{\rm D}^2+\varepsilon_{\rm off}^2+\varepsilon_{\rm sym}^2.
}
\label{eq:energy_partition}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Direct entry formulas in the adapted basis}

Now transform to the corrected local orthonormal basis
\[
t=\frac{1}{\sqrt{11}}(1,-3,1),\qquad
n_1=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,0,-1),\qquad
n_2=\frac{1}{\sqrt{22}}(3,2,3),
\]
and let
\[
B=(t\,|\,n_1\,|\,n_2)\in O(3).
\]

Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde R_f:=B^TR_fB=
\begin{pmatrix}
\tilde r_{11}&\tilde r_{12}&\tilde r_{13}\\
\tilde r_{21}&\tilde r_{22}&\tilde r_{23}\\
\tilde r_{31}&\tilde r_{32}&\tilde r_{33}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

Because orthogonal transformations preserve the Frobenius norm,
\[
\|\widetilde R_f\|_F^2=\|R_f\|_F^2=S_f.
\]

The tangent-transverse mixing fraction is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}^2
=
\frac{
\tilde r_{12}^2+\tilde r_{13}^2+\tilde r_{21}^2+\tilde r_{31}^2
}{
S_f
}.
}
\label{eq:epsmix_entry}
\end{equation}

The pure transverse-block fraction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\perp}^2
=
\frac{
\tilde r_{22}^2+\tilde r_{23}^2+\tilde r_{32}^2+\tilde r_{33}^2
}{
S_f
}.
}
\end{equation}

The pure tangent fraction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{t}^2
=
\frac{\tilde r_{11}^2}{S_f}.
}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
1=\varepsilon_t^2+\varepsilon_{\rm mix}^2+\varepsilon_{\perp}^2.
}
\label{eq:adapted_partition}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Exact threshold meaning for \texorpdfstring{$\tau_{\rm cert}=0.2$}{tau=0.2}}

Fix the certificate tolerance
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\tau_{\rm cert}=0.2.
}
\end{equation}

Then the conditions become immediately interpretable:

\paragraph{Diagonal coarse correction sufficient}
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}\le 0.2
\]
is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{12}^2+r_{13}^2+r_{21}^2+r_{23}^2+r_{31}^2+r_{32}^2
\le
0.04\,S_f.
}
\end{equation}
So at least \(96\%\) of the remainder energy lies on the diagonal.

\paragraph{Full symmetric coarse correction sufficient}
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le 0.2
\]
is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(r_{12}-r_{21})^2+(r_{13}-r_{31})^2+(r_{23}-r_{32})^2
\le
0.08\,S_f.
}
\end{equation}
So at least \(96\%\) of the remainder energy is symmetric.

\paragraph{Coarse branch picture survives in the adapted basis}
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}\le 0.2
\]
is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\tilde r_{12}^2+\tilde r_{13}^2+\tilde r_{21}^2+\tilde r_{31}^2
\le
0.04\,S_f.
}
\end{equation}
So at least \(96\%\) of the remainder energy does not mix the branch tangent with the transverse plane.

\section{5. One-line classification theorem}

\begin{theorem}[One-line classification theorem]
Let
\[
R_f=J_f-J_f^{(4)}
\]
be the extracted Jacobian remainder at the corrected seed, and define
\[
\alpha_f=\frac{\|R_f\|_2}{\lambda_*},
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm diag},
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm sym},
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}
\]
by \eqref{eq:epsdiag_entry}, \eqref{eq:epssym_entry}, and \eqref{eq:epsmix_entry}. Fix \(\tau_{\rm cert}=0.2\). Then the next correct local refinement is determined exactly as follows:

\begin{enumerate}
\item If
\[
\alpha_f\ge 1,
\]
then the quartic baseline no longer controls even invertibility, so a quartic-dominance interpretation must be abandoned immediately.

\item If
\[
\alpha_f<1,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}>0.2,
\]
then the local reduced residual map is genuinely non-gradient at \(20\%\) accuracy, so a symmetric reduced free-energy correction is not valid.

\item If
\[
\alpha_f<1,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le 0.2,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}>0.2,
\]
then the coarse \((A,E,O)\) branch basis fails locally, and sign-resolved suborbit refinement is the correct next move.

\item If
\[
\alpha_f<1,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le 0.2,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}\le 0.2,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}\le 0.2,
\]
then an orbitwise diagonal quadratic normalization layer is sufficient.

\item If
\[
\alpha_f<1,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le 0.2,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}\le 0.2,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}>0.2,
\]
then the correct next model is a full symmetric coarse \(3\times 3\) quadratic layer.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The statement follows from the exact orthogonal decompositions
\[
1=\varepsilon_{\rm D}^2+\varepsilon_{\rm off}^2+\varepsilon_{\rm sym}^2
\]
in the coarse basis and
\[
1=\varepsilon_t^2+\varepsilon_{\rm mix}^2+\varepsilon_{\perp}^2
\]
in the adapted basis, together with the perturbative invertibility threshold \(\alpha_f<1\).
\end{proof}

\section{6. Practical evaluation order}

The next extraction should therefore be evaluated in the following exact order:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_f
\;\Longrightarrow\;
R_f
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\alpha_f
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}.
}
\end{equation}

The reason for this order is logical:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(\alpha_f\) decides whether quartic invertibility control survives at all.
\item \(\varepsilon_{\rm sym}\) decides whether a gradient-like coarse correction is even meaningful.
\item \(\varepsilon_{\rm mix}\) decides whether the coarse branch basis survives locally.
\item \(\varepsilon_{\rm diag}\) only matters after the previous two tests pass.
\end{enumerate}

\section{7. Honest interpretation}

Because the vector-level theorem already gave
\[
\frac{\|G_f-G_f^{(4)}\|}{\|G_f^{(4)}\|}
\ge
0.8496431059127669,
\]
the only viable weak notion of quartic-local sufficiency is:

\[
\boxed{
\text{quartic baseline may still dominate the Jacobian type, even though it does not dominate the corrected residual vector.}
}
\]

So the next local frontier is no longer “is the corrected branch almost quartic?”  
That is already false.

The remaining local frontier is exactly:
\[
\boxed{
\text{what matrix type does }R_f\text{ have?}
}
\]

\section{Final summary}

Once \(J_f\) is extracted, the next step is mathematically automatic.

Compute
\[
R_f=J_f-J_f^{(4)},
\]
then evaluate
\[
\alpha_f,\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm sym},\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm mix},\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}.
\]

With \(\tau_{\rm cert}=0.2\), this gives an exact one-line branching rule:

\[
\alpha_f\ge 1
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\text{quartic baseline loses control;}
\]
\[
\alpha_f<1,\ \varepsilon_{\rm sym}>0.2
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\text{non-gradient local residual map;}
\]
\[
\alpha_f<1,\ \varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le0.2,\ \varepsilon_{\rm mix}>0.2
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\text{suborbit refinement;}
\]
\[
\alpha_f<1,\ \varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le0.2,\ \varepsilon_{\rm mix}\le0.2,\ \varepsilon_{\rm diag}\le0.2
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\text{diagonal coarse quadratic layer;}
\]
\[
\alpha_f<1,\ \varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le0.2,\ \varepsilon_{\rm mix}\le0.2,\ \varepsilon_{\rm diag}>0.2
\;\Longrightarrow\;
\text{full symmetric coarse }3\times 3\text{ layer.}
\]

\section{Final summary}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Current status: the next branch after extracting }J_f\text{ is now fixed by an exact one-line norm classification of }R_f=J_f-J_f^{(4)}.
}
\end{equation}

The corrected stage is frozen at
\[
(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62),
\qquad
\delta_f=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096),
\]
and the correct reduced object is the projected residual map

G(\delta)=\bigl(G_A(\delta),G_E(\delta),G_O(\delta)\bigr)^T.

The corrected projection coefficient sheet must still be interpreted honestly as a residual-based effective reduced coefficient set of the current solver family, not yet as theorem-level microscopic coefficients of a fully closed energy functional. :contentReference[oaicite:1]{index=1}

Because strong quartic-local sufficiency is already excluded at vector level, the only remaining local unknown is the matrix type of
\[
R_f:=J_f-J_f^{(4)}.
\]

Writing
\[
R_f=(r_{ij})_{i,j=1}^3,
\qquad
S_f=\|R_f\|_F^2,
\]
the exact direct formulas are
\[
\alpha_f=\frac{\|R_f\|_2}{\lambda_*},

\[
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}^2
=
\frac{
r_{12}^2+r_{13}^2+r_{21}^2+r_{23}^2+r_{31}^2+r_{32}^2
}{S_f},
\]
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}^2
=
\frac{
(r_{12}-r_{21})^2+(r_{13}-r_{31})^2+(r_{23}-r_{32})^2
}{2S_f},
\]
and in the adapted basis \(\widetilde R_f=B^TR_fB\),
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}^2
=
\frac{
\tilde r_{12}^2+\tilde r_{13}^2+\tilde r_{21}^2+\tilde r_{31}^2
}{S_f}.
\]

With the certificate tolerance \(\tau_{\rm cert}=0.2\), the next branch is determined exactly by:

\[
\alpha_f\ge1
\Longrightarrow
\text{quartic baseline loses invertibility control;}
\]
\[
\alpha_f<1,\ \varepsilon_{\rm sym}>0.2
\Longrightarrow
\text{non-gradient local residual map;}
\]
\[
\alpha_f<1,\ \varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le0.2,\ \varepsilon_{\rm mix}>0.2
\Longrightarrow
\text{sign-resolved suborbit refinement;}
\]
\[
\alpha_f<1,\ \varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le0.2,\ \varepsilon_{\rm mix}\le0.2,\ \varepsilon_{\rm diag}\le0.2
\Longrightarrow
\text{diagonal coarse quadratic layer;}
\]

\alpha_f<1,\ \varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le0.2,\ \varepsilon_{\rm mix}\le0.2,\ \varepsilon_{\rm diag}>0.2
\Longrightarrow
\text{full symmetric coarse }3\times3\text{ quadratic layer.}
\]

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Goal C: extract }J_f\text{ and form }R_f=J_f-J_f^{(4)}.
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Goal M: compute }(\alpha_f,\varepsilon_{\rm sym},\varepsilon_{\rm mix},\varepsilon_{\rm diag}).
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Goal S: branch uniquely to diagonal coarse correction, full symmetric coarse correction, non-gradient residual dynamics, or suborbit refinement.}

\section{Entry-Only No-Eigensolver Certificate for the Jacobian Remainder}

\section{Short explanation}

At the corrected residual stage, the frozen local object is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_f=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096),
\qquad
G(\delta)=
\begin{pmatrix}
G_A(\delta)\\
G_E(\delta)\\
G_O(\delta)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

The exact quartic baseline Jacobian is already known:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_f^{(4)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
10.095240102467715 & -4.991665534361308 & 0.41377801570768584\\
-4.991665534361308 & 22.64650843997611 & -1.2413340471230576\\
0.41377801570768584 & -1.2413340471230576 & 3.6033950146440785
\end{pmatrix},
}
\end{equation}
with smallest eigenvalue
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_*:=\lambda_{\min}(J_f^{(4)})\approx 3.5212959.
}
\end{equation}

After extracting the full local Jacobian
\[
J_f:=DG(\delta_f),
\]
the only remaining local matrix uncertainty is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_f:=J_f-J_f^{(4)}.
}
\end{equation}

The purpose of this section is to provide a fully entry-level certificate for \(R_f\), so that the next refinement branch can be chosen without any spectral decomposition.

\section{1. Entry notation}

Write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
R_f=
\begin{pmatrix}
r_{11}&r_{12}&r_{13}\\
r_{21}&r_{22}&r_{23}\\
r_{31}&r_{32}&r_{33}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

Define the total Frobenius energy
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_f:=\|R_f\|_F^2
=
r_{11}^2+r_{22}^2+r_{33}^2
+
r_{12}^2+r_{13}^2+r_{21}^2+r_{23}^2+r_{31}^2+r_{32}^2.
}
\end{equation}

If \(S_f=0\), then \(R_f=0\) exactly and the local Jacobian is already equal to the quartic baseline.
So from now on assume
\[
S_f>0.
\]

\section{2. A no-eigensolver size parameter}

The exact perturbative size parameter is
\[
\alpha_f=\|R_f\|_2/\lambda_*.
\]
Since
\[
\|R_f\|_2\le \|R_f\|_F=\sqrt{S_f},
\]
we obtain the computable upper bound
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha_f
\le
\widehat\alpha_f
:=
\frac{\sqrt{S_f}}{\lambda_*}.
}
\end{equation}

This gives the exact sufficient invertibility certificate:

\begin{theorem}[No-eigensolver invertibility certificate]
If
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat\alpha_f<1,
}
\end{equation}
then automatically \(\alpha_f<1\), hence \(J_f\) is invertible.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from \(\|R_f\|_2\le \|R_f\|_F\).
\end{proof}

Numerically,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat\alpha_f<1
\iff
S_f<\lambda_*^2\approx 12.39952282135081.
}
\end{equation}

Likewise, the strong and moderate Jacobian-dominance regimes admit the entry-only sufficient conditions
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat\alpha_f\le 0.2
\iff
S_f\le 0.04\,\lambda_*^2\approx 0.4959809128540324,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat\alpha_f\le 0.5
\iff
S_f\le 0.25\,\lambda_*^2\approx 3.0998807053377026.
}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Exact coarse-basis decomposition}

Define the diagonal part
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D_f:=\operatorname{diag}(r_{11},r_{22},r_{33}).
}
\end{equation}

Define the symmetric off-diagonal part
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_f:=
\frac12(R_f+R_f^T)-D_f
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \frac{r_{12}+r_{21}}{2} & \frac{r_{13}+r_{31}}{2}\\[2mm]
\frac{r_{12}+r_{21}}{2} & 0 & \frac{r_{23}+r_{32}}{2}\\[2mm]
\frac{r_{13}+r_{31}}{2} & \frac{r_{23}+r_{32}}{2} & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

Define the antisymmetric part
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_f:=
\frac12(R_f-R_f^T)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0 & \frac{r_{12}-r_{21}}{2} & \frac{r_{13}-r_{31}}{2}\\[2mm]
-\frac{r_{12}-r_{21}}{2} & 0 & \frac{r_{23}-r_{32}}{2}\\[2mm]
-\frac{r_{13}-r_{31}}{2} & -\frac{r_{23}-r_{32}}{2} & 0
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

Then
\[
R_f=D_f+C_f+A_f,
\]
and these three subspaces are Frobenius-orthogonal.

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_f=\|D_f\|_F^2+\|C_f\|_F^2+\|A_f\|_F^2.
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Closed entry formulas for the classification fractions}

The diagonal-fit defect is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}^2
=
\frac{
r_{12}^2+r_{13}^2+r_{21}^2+r_{23}^2+r_{31}^2+r_{32}^2
}{
S_f
}.
}
\end{equation}

The skew fraction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}^2
=
\frac{
(r_{12}-r_{21})^2+(r_{13}-r_{31})^2+(r_{23}-r_{32})^2
}{
2S_f
}.
}
\end{equation}

The pure symmetric off-diagonal fraction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm off}^2
=
\frac{
(r_{12}+r_{21})^2+(r_{13}+r_{31})^2+(r_{23}+r_{32})^2
}{
2S_f
}.
}
\end{equation}

The diagonal energy fraction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_D^2
=
\frac{r_{11}^2+r_{22}^2+r_{33}^2}{S_f}.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact partition identity is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
1=\varepsilon_D^2+\varepsilon_{\rm off}^2+\varepsilon_{\rm sym}^2.
}
\end{equation}

\paragraph{Interpretation.}
\begin{itemize}
\item \(\varepsilon_{\rm diag}\) measures how far \(R_f\) is from a diagonal coarse correction.
\item \(\varepsilon_{\rm sym}\) measures how far \(R_f\) is from a symmetric coarse correction.
\item \(\varepsilon_{\rm off}\) measures the genuinely symmetric off-diagonal coarse structure.
\end{itemize}

\section{5. Exact adapted-basis formulas}

Use the orthonormal corrected local basis
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
t=\frac{1}{\sqrt{11}}(1,-3,1),
\qquad
n_1=\frac{1}{\sqrt2}(1,0,-1),
\qquad
n_2=\frac{1}{\sqrt{22}}(3,2,3),
}
\end{equation}
and define
\[
B=(t\,|\,n_1\,|\,n_2)\in O(3).
\]

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde R_f:=B^T R_f B=(\tilde r_{ij})_{i,j=1}^3.
}
\end{equation}

The four entries relevant for tangent-transverse mixing are:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\tilde r_{12}
=
\frac{(r_{11}-r_{13})-3(r_{21}-r_{23})+(r_{31}-r_{33})}{\sqrt{22}},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\tilde r_{21}
=
\frac{(r_{11}-3r_{12}+r_{13})-(r_{31}-3r_{32}+r_{33})}{\sqrt{22}},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\tilde r_{13}
=
\frac{
(3r_{11}+2r_{12}+3r_{13})
-3(3r_{21}+2r_{22}+3r_{23})
+(3r_{31}+2r_{32}+3r_{33})
}{\sqrt{242}},
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\tilde r_{31}
=
\frac{
(3r_{11}-9r_{12}+3r_{13})
+2(3r_{21}-9r_{22}+3r_{23})
+(3r_{31}-9r_{32}+3r_{33})
}{\sqrt{242}}.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the tangent-transverse mixing fraction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}^2
=
\frac{
\tilde r_{12}^2+\tilde r_{13}^2+\tilde r_{21}^2+\tilde r_{31}^2
}{S_f}.
}
\end{equation}

This uses only the entries \(r_{ij}\).

\section{6. Threshold meaning for \texorpdfstring{$\tau_{\rm cert}=0.2$}{tau=0.2}}

Fix
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\tau_{\rm cert}=0.2.
}
\end{equation}

Then:

\paragraph{Diagonal coarse quadratic layer sufficient}
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}\le 0.2
\]
is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_{12}^2+r_{13}^2+r_{21}^2+r_{23}^2+r_{31}^2+r_{32}^2
\le
0.04\,S_f.
}
\end{equation}
So at least \(96\%\) of the remainder energy lies on the diagonal.

\paragraph{Full symmetric coarse \(3\times 3\) layer sufficient}
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le 0.2
\]
is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(r_{12}-r_{21})^2+(r_{13}-r_{31})^2+(r_{23}-r_{32})^2
\le
0.08\,S_f.
}
\end{equation}
So at least \(96\%\) of the remainder energy is symmetric.

\paragraph{Coarse branch basis survives locally}
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}\le 0.2
\]
is equivalent to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\tilde r_{12}^2+\tilde r_{13}^2+\tilde r_{21}^2+\tilde r_{31}^2
\le
0.04\,S_f.
}
\end{equation}
So at least \(96\%\) of the remainder energy does not mix the corrected tangent direction with the transverse plane.

\section{7. One-line decision theorem}

\begin{theorem}[Entry-only one-line decision theorem]
Let \(J_f\) be the extracted local residual Jacobian at the corrected seed and define
\[
R_f:=J_f-J_f^{(4)}.
\]
Compute \(S_f\), \(\widehat\alpha_f\), \(\varepsilon_{\rm sym}\), \(\varepsilon_{\rm mix}\), and \(\varepsilon_{\rm diag}\) from the entry formulas above.

Then, with \(\tau_{\rm cert}=0.2\), the correct next reduced refinement is determined as follows:

\begin{enumerate}
\item If
\[
\widehat\alpha_f\ge 1,
\]
then quartic baseline control of invertibility is no longer guaranteed, so quartic Jacobian dominance must be abandoned immediately.

\item If
\[
\widehat\alpha_f<1,
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}>0.2,
\]
then the local reduced residual map is genuinely non-gradient at \(20\%\) accuracy, so a symmetric reduced free-energy correction is not valid.

\item If
\[
\widehat\alpha_f<1,
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le 0.2,
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}>0.2,
\]
then the coarse \((A,E,O)\) branch picture fails locally and sign-resolved suborbit refinement is the correct next move.

\item If
\[
\widehat\alpha_f<1,
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le 0.2,
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}\le 0.2,
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}\le 0.2,
\]
then an orbitwise diagonal quadratic normalization layer is sufficient.

\item If
\[
\widehat\alpha_f<1,
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}\le 0.2,
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}\le 0.2,
\qquad
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}>0.2,
\]
then the correct next reduced model is a full symmetric coarse \(3\times 3\) quadratic layer.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
All statements follow from the exact orthogonal Frobenius decomposition of \(R_f\), the explicit adapted-basis mixing formulas, and the sufficient invertibility certificate \(\widehat\alpha_f<1\).
\end{proof}

\section{8. Practical evaluation order}

The next extraction should therefore be evaluated in the exact order
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_f
\Longrightarrow
R_f
\Longrightarrow
S_f
\Longrightarrow
\widehat\alpha_f
\Longrightarrow
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}
\Longrightarrow
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}
\Longrightarrow
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}.
}
\end{equation}

This order is logically minimal:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(S_f\) gives the no-eigensolver size bound.
\item \(\widehat\alpha_f\) decides whether quartic invertibility control survives.
\item \(\varepsilon_{\rm sym}\) decides whether a symmetric reduced free-energy interpretation survives.
\item \(\varepsilon_{\rm mix}\) decides whether the coarse branch basis survives.
\item \(\varepsilon_{\rm diag}\) distinguishes diagonal versus full symmetric coarse correction.
\end{enumerate}

\section{Final summary}

After extracting \(J_f\), the next branch is no longer ambiguous.

Write
\[
R_f=J_f-J_f^{(4)}=(r_{ij})_{i,j=1}^3,
\qquad
S_f=\|R_f\|_F^2.
\]
Then compute directly from the entries:
\[
\widehat\alpha_f=\frac{\sqrt{S_f}}{\lambda_*},
\]
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm sym}^2
=
\frac{
(r_{12}-r_{21})^2+(r_{13}-r_{31})^2+(r_{23}-r_{32})^2
}{2S_f},
\]
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm diag}^2
=
\frac{
r_{12}^2+r_{13}^2+r_{21}^2+r_{23}^2+r_{31}^2+r_{32}^2
}{S_f},
\]
and
\[
\varepsilon_{\rm mix}^2
=
\frac{
\tilde r_{12}^2+\tilde r_{13}^2+\tilde r_{21}^2+\tilde r_{31}^2
}{S_f},
\]
with \(\tilde r_{12},\tilde r_{13},\tilde r_{21},\tilde r_{31}\) given explicitly above.

Thus the next local refinement is decided by one line of arithmetic:
\[
\boxed{
(\widehat\alpha_f,\varepsilon_{\rm sym},\varepsilon_{\rm mix},\varepsilon_{\rm diag}).
}
\]

\section{Immediate Next Step: Refined Four-Variable Residual Closure}

\section{Why we stop chasing the unavailable Jacobian}

At the current corrected residual stage, the true bottleneck is no longer the carrier-side witness and no longer the failed \((u,v,\kappa)\) shell compression.
The files already fix the correct reduced object as the projected residual map
\[
G(\delta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
G_A(\delta)\\
G_E(\delta)\\
G_O(\delta)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
and also show that Newton/damped-Newton updates are not geometry-preserving on the BCC branch.
Therefore the correct next move is not to keep chasing an unavailable full Jacobian \(J_f\), but to enlarge the residual-level orbit basis itself. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6} 

\section{Refined orbit split}

The minimal nonredundant refinement beyond the coarse \((A,E,O)\) split is
\[
(A,E,O_+,O_-),
\]
where
\[
A=\{\pm(1,1,0)/\sqrt2\},
\qquad
E=\{\pm(1,-1,0)/\sqrt2\},
\]
\[
O_+=\{\pm(1,0,1)/\sqrt2,\ \pm(0,1,1)/\sqrt2\},
\qquad
O_-=\{\pm(1,0,-1)/\sqrt2,\ \pm(0,1,-1)/\sqrt2\}.
\]

The group sizes are
\[
n_A=2,\qquad n_E=2,\qquad n_{O_+}=4,\qquad n_{O_-}=4.
\]

\section{Exact refined quartic matrix}

Using the already extracted corrected four-class shell coefficients
\[
u_d=2493.1087739398513,\quad
u_{\rm opp}=14874.171297437068,\quad
u_\perp=9027.17290917827,\quad
u_{\rm obl}=2244.8894311890813,
\]
the normalized refined quartic matrix is exactly
\[
\boxed{
\bar M^{(4)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}

9027.17290917827 & 8683.640035688459 & 2244.8894311890813 & 2244.8894311890813\\
2244.8894311890813 & 2244.8894311890813 & 5464.26473343877 & 5636.031170183676\\
2244.8894311890813 & 2244.8894311890813 & 5636.031170183676 & 5464.26473343877
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

\section{Refined corrected seed and quartic load}

\]

Then

\end{pmatrix}.

Hence the quartic residual vector is

\boxed{
G^{(4)}_{(4{\rm var})}(x_f)
=

}

\section{Refined quartic Jacobian}

The quartic Jacobian in the refined four-variable model is
\[
J_{IJ}^{(4,4)}(x)
=
\delta_{IJ}Q_I(x)+2x_I\bar M^{(4)}_{IJ}x_J.
\]

At the lifted corrected seed \(x_f\), this gives
\[
\boxed{
J_f^{(4,4)}=
\begin{pmatrix}
10.302129114812741 & -4.991665531859216 & 0.4137780199567714 & 0.4137780199567714\\
-4.991665531859216 & 22.853397448870943 & -1.2413340598703142 & -1.2413340598703142\\
0.4137780199567714 & -1.2413340598703142 & 4.099066645929136 & 1.038833265288255\\
0.4137780199567714 & -1.2413340598703142 & 1.038833265288255 & 4.099066645929136
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\]

The antisymmetric oblique-splitting mode
\[
v_{O{\rm split}}=(0,0,1,-1)
\]
is an exact eigenvector with eigenvalue
\[
\boxed{
\lambda_{O{\rm split}}^{(4)}=3.060233380640881>0.
}
\]

So the \(O_+-O_-\) splitting channel is real and dynamically meaningful already at quartic level.

\section{Immediate research decision}

Therefore the correct next step is now fixed:

\[
\boxed{
\text{stop chasing the unavailable }J_f,
\qquad
\text{upgrade immediately from coarse }(A,E,O)\text{ to refined }(A,E,O_+,O_-).

with quartic part

The correct solver is not Newton.
It is geometry-constrained residual minimization inside the admissible BCC shell-retaining basin.

\section{Short explanation}

\section{5. Symmetric / antisymmetric oblique decomposition}

Introduce
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s:=\frac{o_++o_-}{2},
\qquad

\qquad
o_+=s+d,\quad o_-=s-d.

\end{equation}

Then the oblique quartic loads become
\begin{align}
Q_{O_+}
&=
m_{AO}(a^2+e^2)
+
(m_d+m_c)(s^2+d^2)
+
2(m_d-m_c)sd,
\\
Q_{O_-}
&=
m_{AO}(a^2+e^2)
+
(m_d+m_c)(s^2+d^2)
-
2(m_d-m_c)sd,
\end{align}
where
\[
m_{AO}=2244.8894311890813,
\qquad
m_d=5464.26473343877,
\qquad
m_c=5636.031170183676.
\]

Define the symmetric and antisymmetric residual combinations
\[
G_s:=\frac{G_{O_+}+G_{O_-}}{2},
\qquad
G_d:=\frac{G_{O_+}-G_{O_-}}{2}.
\]
A direct expansion gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_s
=
s\Bigl(
m_{AO}(a^2+e^2)
+
(m_d+m_c)s^2
+
(3m_d-m_c)d^2
\Bigr),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_d
=
d\Bigl(
m_{AO}(a^2+e^2)
+
(m_d+m_c)d^2
+
(3m_d-m_c)s^2
\Bigr).
}
\end{equation}

Since
\[
m_d+m_c=11100.295903622446,
\qquad
3m_d-m_c=10756.763030132635,
\]
both channels are strictly cubic-stiff at quartic level.

\section{6. Corrected symmetric point and the oblique-splitting mode}

At the lifted corrected seed,
\[
s=0.0096,\qquad d=0,
\]
so automatically
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_d(x_f)=0.
}
\end{equation}

Moreover the linearization of the antisymmetric mode is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left.\frac{\partial G_d}{\partial d}\right|_{x_f}
=
m_{AO}(a^2+e^2)+(3m_d-m_c)s^2.
}
\end{equation}

Substituting the corrected values gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_{d}^{(4)}
=
3.060233380640881>0.
}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the \(4\times4\) Jacobian, the vector
\[

is an exact eigenvector:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

=
3.060233380640881\,v_d.
}
\end{equation}

So the oblique-splitting mode is real and dynamically meaningful, but it is \emph{stabilized} at the symmetric corrected point.

\section{7. Sharp consequence}

This calculation closes the quartic part of the refined orbit problem.

\begin{theorem}[Quartic refined no-splitting theorem at the corrected symmetric point]
In the refined four-variable quartic residual model

Therefore the quartic refined shell kernel by itself does not drive \(O_+-O_-\) splitting away from the symmetric corrected branch.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Immediate from the explicit formula for \(G_d\) and the linearized coefficient above.
\end{proof}

\section{Source-by-Source Microscopic Closure of the \(TD+DT\) Transverse Audit}

\section{Short explanation}

At the present sharpest explicit working-branch level, the coefficient-routing problem is already structurally closed.

The longitudinal coefficient is extracted from the \(OO\)-block:
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\]
while the transverse even/odd pair is extracted from the mixed transverse block:
\[
\mathcal H_{TD}+\mathcal H_{DT}\to \Lambda_E,\Lambda_O.
\]

More sharply, on the current explicit Class II witness route,
\[
JJ \to \lambda_c,
\qquad
JK+KJ \to (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
\qquad
KK \to \text{same-shell residual transverse corrections}.
\]

Therefore the remaining task is not conceptual theorem-building.
It is the literal evaluation of the background-linearized first-order Hessian kernels
\[
\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}(\xi)+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}(\xi),
\]
on the frozen corrected branch. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5} :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\section{1. Exact source split after Schur reduction}

After integrating out the heavy mediator, the quadratic correction has the exact split
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_X^{(2)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\delta J\,\delta J^\dagger
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\bigl(\delta J\,\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\,\delta J^\dagger\bigr)
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,\delta K\,\delta K^\dagger.
}
\label{eq:TDDT_source_split}
\end{equation}

Thus the microscopic source sectors are
\[
JJ,\qquad JK+KJ,\qquad KK.
\]

The current branch-level routing is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ \leftrightarrow OO\text{-longitudinal audit},
\qquad
JK+KJ \leftrightarrow TD+DT\text{-transverse audit}.
}
\label{eq:TDDT_routing}
\end{equation}

At principal order, the \(KK\)-sector is not the primitive longitudinal source and should be treated as a transverse residual/completion correction sector. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8} :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

\section{2. Longitudinal side is already isolated}

On the intended Class II-compatible branch,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_\parallel^{(0)}=0,
}
\end{equation}
so the practical longitudinal coefficient is Branch B:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_c
=
2\lim_{\theta'\to0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]}{\theta'(\xi)^3},
\qquad
V^\mu_{OO}:=\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}\,\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:lambda_c_OO}
\end{equation}

Therefore the longitudinal routing is not the current ambiguity.

The current ambiguity is the transverse pair
\[
\Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10} :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\section{3. Exact \(TD+DT\) transverse carrier}

Define the mixed first-order transverse carrier
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
:=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q.
}
\label{eq:MTDDT_def}
\end{equation}

The leading even/odd coefficient point is extracted by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}].
}
\label{eq:LambdaEO_proj}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in the leading mixed-block truncation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
e_0^{(1)}=\Lambda_E,
\qquad
o_0^{(1)}=\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:e0o0_to_Lambda}
\end{equation}

At the branch-summary level, the leading transverse kernel has the invariant form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\theta'(\xi)\Bigl[
\Lambda_E\,E^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
+
\Lambda_O\,J^\mu{}_a\Sigma_a
\Bigr]
+
\mathcal M^\mu_{\rm corr},
}
\label{eq:MTDDT_invariant_form}
\end{equation}
where \(\mathcal M^\mu_{\rm corr}\) starts at higher order and/or completion channels such as
\[
OD,\quad DO,\quad DD.
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12} :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

\section{4. Why the naive local \(JK\) statement is too strong}

The crucial caveat is that a naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear does not automatically generate the transverse pair.

In the shell-adapted Pauli basis,
\[
J\sim j\,\Sigma_3,
\qquad
K\sim k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2.
\]
Then the simplest local real Hermitian bilinear gives
\begin{align}
\Sigma_3(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)
+
(k_E\Sigma_1+k_O\Sigma_2)\Sigma_3
&=
k_E\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_1\}+k_O\{\Sigma_3,\Sigma_2\}
\\
&=0.
\end{align}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the naive local real Hermitian }JK\text{ bilinear vanishes.}
}
\label{eq:naiveJKzero}
\end{equation}

So the statement
\[
JK\text{ alone automatically gives }(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)
\]
is too strong.

What is actually load-bearing is the derivative-resolved shell audit
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{JK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
\qquad
\partial_{p_\nu}\widehat\Sigma_{KK}(G_*;p)\big|_{p=0},
}
\label{eq:derivative_audit}
\end{equation}
or, in the explicit folded-Bragg Class II bookkeeping,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat T^\alpha_{(II)}(G_*)
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\sum_A\sum_{Q+Q'=G_*}
\widehat J_i^A(Q)\widehat K_{i,\alpha}^A(Q').
}
\label{eq:foldedBragg_Talpha}
\end{equation}

Thus the real transverse frontier is the explicit differentiated kernel, not a local algebraic \(JK\) shortcut. :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14}

\section{5. Exact projector formulas for the matrix entries}

Let the projected \(Q_B\)-valued mixed carrier be represented in the Pauli basis as
\begin{equation}
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
m_0^\mu\,\mathbf 1_2
+
m_a^\mu\,\Sigma_a.
\end{equation}

Then the invariant projectors read
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 E^\mu{}_a \Tr(\Sigma_a \mathcal M_\mu),
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M]
=
\frac14 J^\mu{}_a \Tr(\Sigma_a \mathcal M_\mu).
}
\label{eq:PEPO_def}
\end{equation}

If one writes the \(Q_B\)-matrix entries as
\[
r_{11},\qquad r_{22},\qquad r_{12},
\]
then the Pauli components are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
s_3=\frac{r_{11}-r_{22}}{2},
\qquad
s_1=\Re r_{12},
\qquad
s_2=-\Im r_{12}.
}
\label{eq:s123_def}
\end{equation}

The longitudinal \(OO\)-projection reads \(s_3\), whereas the transverse \(TD+DT\)-projection reads \(s_1,s_2\), i.e.
\[
\Lambda_E,\qquad \Lambda_O.
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:15]{index=15}

\section{6. Reduced coefficient dictionary}

Once \(\lambda_c,\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O\) are extracted, the reduced Branch-B coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac12 I_{\theta'^3}\lambda_c,
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:reduced_dict}
\end{equation}

With the explicit overlaps
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
\qquad
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:overlap_values}
\end{equation}
this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\lambda_c\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\Lambda_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:alpha_beta_explicit}
\end{equation}

Therefore the exact microscopic chain is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c \to \lambda_\parallel,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD}+\mathcal H_{DT}\to (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O)\to(\alpha,\beta).
}
\label{eq:exact_chain}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:16]{index=16} :contentReference[oaicite:17]{index=17}

\section{7. What is actually closed and what is still open}

What is already closed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{routing logic is closed: }
OO\to\lambda_c,\qquad TD+DT\to(\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
}
\end{equation}

What is also closed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ\text{ is the unique principal longitudinal source,}
\qquad
JK+KJ\text{ is the principal transverse source,}
}
\end{equation}
while
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
KK\text{ is a transverse residual/completion sector, not the principal carrier source.}
}
\end{equation}

What remains open is not conceptual structure, but the literal evaluation of
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}(\xi)+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}(\xi)
}
\end{equation}
on the frozen corrected branch. :contentReference[oaicite:18]{index=18} :contentReference[oaicite:19]{index=19}

\section{8. Executable next microscopic step}

The next executable calculation is therefore uniquely fixed:

\begin{enumerate}
\item write the explicit background-linearized kernels

\delta J,\qquad \delta K
\]
on the frozen corrected branch;

\item evaluate the \(OO\)-projection
\[
V^\mu_{OO}=\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}\,\Pi_Q

and extract

\lambda_c

\item evaluate the mixed projection

\]
and extract
\[
\Lambda_E=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}];
\]

\item only after that, return to the residual-level enlarged-kernel rerun.
\end{enumerate}

So the next frontier is a literal source-by-source Hessian differentiation and projection computation, not another abstract reduction theorem. :contentReference[oaicite:20]{index=20} :contentReference[oaicite:21]{index=21}

\section{Final summary}

The remaining coefficient point on the current explicit Class II working branch is

The exact routing is

The naive local real Hermitian \(JK\) bilinear vanishes, so a nonzero transverse pair requires derivative-resolved and/or phase-resolved microscopic structure.

It is the explicit evaluation of
\[
\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}(\xi),
\qquad
\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}(\xi)+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}(\xi)

on the frozen corrected branch and the corresponding projector traces.

\section{Load-Bearing \texorpdfstring{$\delta J,\delta K$}{delta J, delta K} Audit on the Frozen Corrected Branch}

\section{Goal}

At the current sharpest explicit working-branch level, the routing problem is already closed:
\[
\mathcal H_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
\mathcal H_{TD}+\mathcal H_{DT}\to (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
\]
So the next task is no longer abstract theorem-building.
It is the literal background-linearized evaluation of the load-bearing currents
\[
\delta J,\qquad \delta K
\]
on the frozen corrected branch and the extraction of the first active transverse odd source.

\section{1. Frozen working branch and exact source split}

We keep fixed the explicit Class II working branch
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^a J_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^a K_i^a[P,\Psi].
}
\label{eq:LB_working_branch}
\end{equation}

The heavy mediator is algebraic:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_i^a
=
-\frac{1}{M_X^2}\Bigl(\alpha_X J_i^a+\beta_X K_i^a\Bigr).
}
\label{eq:LB_Xelim}
\end{equation}

Substituting back gives the exact tree-level effective interaction
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(X)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{2M_X^2}J_i^aJ_i^a
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}J_i^aK_i^a
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{2M_X^2}K_i^aK_i^a.
}
\label{eq:LB_Leff}
\end{equation}

Thus the exact source decomposition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ,\qquad JK+KJ,\qquad KK.
}
\label{eq:LB_source_split}
\end{equation}

At the sharp current routing level,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
JK+KJ\to (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
\qquad
KK\to \text{transverse residual corrections}.
}
\label{eq:LB_routing}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Defect-background currents}

Take the locked one-defect background
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_B(\xi,x_\parallel)=\phi_0(x_\parallel)\,z_B(\xi),
\qquad
P_B(\xi)=z_B(\xi)z_B^\dagger(\xi),
\qquad
z_B^\dagger z_B=1.
}
\label{eq:LB_background}
\end{equation}

The microscopic currents are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a[\Psi]
=
(\partial_i\Psi^\dagger)T_a\Psi+\Psi^\dagger T_a(\partial_i\Psi),
}
\label{eq:LB_J_def}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a[P,\psi]
=
\Tr(T_a\partial_iP)\,\mathcal O[\psi].
}
\label{eq:LB_K_def}
\end{equation}

On the defect background one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_i^a[\Psi_B]
=
2(\partial_i\phi_0)\phi_0\,m_a(\theta)
+
\delta_{i\xi}\phi_0^2\,\mathcal A_\xi^a(\theta,\theta'),
}
\label{eq:LB_J_background}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
m_a(\theta)=z_B^\dagger T_a z_B,
\qquad
\mathcal A_\xi^a
=
(\partial_\xi z_B^\dagger)T_a z_B+z_B^\dagger T_a(\partial_\xi z_B),
\label{eq:LB_mA_defs}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_i^a[P_B,\psi]
=
\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,\mathcal O[\psi],
\qquad
k_a(\theta):=\Tr\!\Bigl[T_a(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger)\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:LB_K_background}
\end{equation}

So the background \(J\)-sector is already linear in the shell gradient \(\partial_i\phi_0\), whereas the \(K\)-sector is linear in the defect/projector derivative \(\theta'(\xi)\).

\section{3. Load-bearing linearized kernels}

Around the locked background, the lowest-derivative load-bearing parts can be written in the factorized form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta J_i^a[\Psi_0;\delta\Psi]_{\rm lb}
=
m^a(P_0)\,(\partial_i\phi_0)\,
\mathcal U_{jr}{}^{b}\,(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r,
}
\label{eq:LB_dJ_factorized}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta K_i^a[P_0;\delta\Psi]_{\rm lb}
=
(\partial_i\xi^a)\,
\mathcal V_{jr}{}^{b}\,(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r.
}
\label{eq:LB_dK_factorized}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, before factorization, the general lowest-order load-bearing pieces are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta J_i^a[\Psi_0;\delta\Psi]_{\rm lb}
=
\mathcal B_{jr}^a\,(\partial_i\phi_0)\,(-i\partial_j)\psi_r,
}
\label{eq:LB_dJ_general}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta K_i^a[P_0;\delta\Psi]_{\rm lb}
=
\mathcal F_{ijr}^{ab}\,(\partial_i\xi^a)\,(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r.
}
\label{eq:LB_dK_general}
\end{equation}

These are exactly the \((i,a)\)-carrier structures needed for the one-mediator Schur witness route.

\section{4. Projected transport kernels}

The first-order one-defect Hessian blocks admit the expansion
\begin{equation}
\mathcal H_{AB}
=
\mathcal H_{AB}^{(0)}(\xi)
-
i\,\mathcal V^\mu_{AB}(\xi)\partial_{y^\mu}
+\cdots.
\end{equation}

The longitudinal coefficient is extracted from the \(OO\)-projection:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
V^\mu_{OO}
=
\Pi_Q\,\mathcal V^\mu_{OO}\,\Pi_Q,
\qquad
\lambda_c
=
2\lim_{\theta'\to0}
\frac{\mathfrak P_\parallel[V_{OO}]}{\theta'(\xi)^3}.
}
\label{eq:LB_lambda_c}
\end{equation}

The transverse pair is extracted from the mixed \(TD+DT\)-projection:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal M^\mu_{TD+DT}
=
\Pi_Q\bigl(\mathcal V^\mu_{TD}+\mathcal V^\mu_{DT}\bigr)\Pi_Q,
}
\label{eq:LB_MTDDT}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_E=\mathfrak P_E[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}],
\qquad
\Lambda_O=\mathfrak P_O[\mathcal M_{TD+DT}^{\rm inv}].
}
\label{eq:LB_LambdaEO}
\end{equation}

So after overlap insertion the reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_\theta\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_\theta\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:LB_dictionary}
\end{equation}

\section{5. First active odd transverse source}

At the exact transport-extraction level, the odd transverse source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
X_2(\delta)
=
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\mathcal M^{\rm inv}_{TD+DT}(\delta)
\right].
}
\label{eq:LB_X2}
\end{equation}

Therefore the corrected odd transverse Hessian response is defined by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{rs}
:=
\partial_{\delta_r}\partial_{\delta_s}X_2(\delta)\big|_{\delta=0}
=
\partial_{\delta_r}\partial_{\delta_s}
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\mathcal M^{\rm inv}_{TD+DT}(\delta)
\right]_{\delta=0}.
}
\label{eq:LB_H2_def}
\end{equation}

On the current refined locked \(+\) Class II working branch, the leading mixed-channel realization is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
\partial_{rs}\bigl(
\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger
\bigr)_{\delta=0}
\Big]
+\text{subleading completion terms}.
}
\label{eq:LB_H2_JK}
\end{equation}

This is the decisive result:
the first active odd transverse response on the frozen corrected branch is the quadratic Hessian response of the mixed \(JK+KJ\) channel.

\section{6. Why no linear odd transverse activation occurs at the frozen corrected seed}

On the sign-resolved first-shell lift of the frozen corrected seed, the exact transverse rows satisfy
\[
r^{(ct_1)}_{\rm sub}\!\cdot\!\delta_{\rm sub}^{\rm corr}=0,
\qquad
r^{(ct_2)}_{\rm sub}\!\cdot\!\delta_{\rm sub}^{\rm corr}=0.
\]
Hence the sign-sensitive first-shell transverse factor has no linear corrected shift at the frozen corrected branch.

Therefore the odd transverse coefficient does not turn on linearly in the present orbit-symmetric corrected seed.
Instead, the first genuine odd source is the quadratic response \eqref{eq:LB_H2_JK}.

\section{7. Honest branch-level conclusion}

The \(TD+DT\) audit is now sharp enough to separate what is already closed from what is still open.

What is closed:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
JJ\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
JK+KJ\to (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Lambda_O
\text{ first appears through }
H^{(2)}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
\partial_{rs}\bigl(
\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger
\bigr)_{\delta=0}
\Big]
+\cdots .
}
\end{equation}

What is still open is the literal evaluation of the background-dependent tensors
\[
\mathcal U_{jr}{}^b,
\qquad
\mathcal V_{jr}{}^b,
\qquad
m^a(P_0),
\qquad
\partial_i\xi^a,
\]
on the frozen corrected branch.

So the next executable microscopic task is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{compute the actual matrix }H^{(2)}_{rs}
\text{ from the frozen corrected branch harmonics,}
}
\end{equation}
and then project it by \(\mathfrak P_O\) to decide whether \(\Lambda_O\neq 0\) beyond the rigid first-shell truncation.
\section{Final summary}

The background currents are explicit:
\[
J_i^a[\Psi_B]

The exact extraction problem is

V_{OO}\to\lambda_c,

The first active odd transverse source is not linear in the frozen corrected seed.

\[
H^{(2)}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
\partial_{rs}\bigl(
\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger
\bigr)_{\delta=0}
\Big]
+\cdots .
\]

Thus the next actual microscopic computation is now fixed:
evaluate the matrix \(H^{(2)}_{rs}\) on the frozen corrected branch and decide whether the odd transverse channel is really activated.

\section{Final summary}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Current stage: }TD+DT\text{ projected Hessian audit on the frozen corrected branch.}
}
\end{equation}

The strongest explicit Class II working branch is
\[
L_{\mathrm{mic}}
=
L_{\Psi}^{\mathrm{ref}}[\Psi,P]
+
\frac{M_X^2}{2}X_i^aX_i^a
+
\alpha_X X_i^aJ_i^a[\Psi]
+
\beta_X X_i^aK_i^a[P,\Psi],
\]
and after eliminating the heavy mediator,
\[
L_{\mathrm{eff}}^{(X)}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X^2}{2M_X^2}J_i^aJ_i^a
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}J_i^aK_i^a
-\frac{\beta_X^2}{2M_X^2}K_i^aK_i^a.
\]

The exact routing is
\[
JJ\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
JK+KJ\to (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O),
\qquad
KK\to \text{transverse corrections}.
\]

On the defect background,
\[
J_i^a[\Psi_B]
=
2(\partial_i\phi_0)\phi_0\,m_a(\theta)
+
\delta_{i\xi}\phi_0^2\,\mathcal A_\xi^a(\theta,\theta'),
\]
\[
K_i^a[P_B,\psi]
=
\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta)\,\mathcal O[\psi].
\]

Hence the load-bearing linearized kernels are of the form
\[
\delta J_i^a[\Psi_0;\delta\Psi]_{\rm lb}
=
m^a(P_0)(\partial_i\phi_0)\mathcal U_{jr}{}^b(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r,
\]
\[
\delta K_i^a[P_0;\delta\Psi]_{\rm lb}
=
(\partial_i\xi^a)\mathcal V_{jr}{}^b(-i\partial_j)s_b\psi_r.
\]

The exact extraction problem is
\[
V_{OO}\to \lambda_c,
\qquad
\mathcal M_{TD+DT}\to (\Lambda_E,\Lambda_O).
\]

The first active odd transverse source is
\[
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
\partial_{rs}\bigl(
\delta J\delta K^\dagger+\delta K\delta J^\dagger
\bigr)_{\delta=0}
\Big]
+\text{subleading completion terms}.
}
\]

So the next actual microscopic step is no longer abstract:
\[
\boxed{
\text{compute }H^{(2)}_{rs}\text{ on the frozen corrected branch and decide whether }\Lambda_O\neq0.
}
\]

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Goal C: evaluate the actual background-linearized }OO\text{ and }TD+DT\text{ kernels.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Goal M: compute }H^{(2)}_{rs}\text{ and extract the first nonzero odd transverse source.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Goal S: decide whether the rigid first-shell truncation must be upgraded by non-rigid projector/internal structure or higher-shell completion.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Actual Computation of the First Frozen-Branch Odd Transverse Response}

\section{Short explanation}

We now compute the odd transverse correction as far as the currently available explicit formulas allow.

The working branch is frozen at
\[
\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096)^T,
\]
and the corrected odd transverse coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0\,
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})
+
O(\delta^3),
}
\label{eq:calc_beta_corr_start}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})
=
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{AA}
+
4.1472\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{EE}
+
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{OO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{AE}
+
9.216\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{AO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{EO}.
}
\label{eq:calc_Q2_numeric}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\section{1. Fast six-row formula}

Under the fast practical approximation
\[
J_{rs}\approx 0,\qquad
K_{rs}\approx 0,\qquad
\Delta^{\mathrm{comp}}_{rs}\approx 0,
\]
all six rows reduce to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{rs}
\approx
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_rK_s^\dagger+J_sK_r^\dagger+K_rJ_s^\dagger+K_sJ_r^\dagger
\big].
}
\label{eq:calc_Hfast_general}
\end{equation}
So the problem is reduced to the three orbit-current pairs
\[
(J_A,K_A),\qquad (J_E,K_E),\qquad (J_O,K_O).
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\section{2. Explicit orbit-current pairs}

The completed orbit currents are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{r,i}^a
=
q_0^a\,\partial_iN_r
+
(\partial_i\bar\rho)(\eta_r c^a+\bar\eta_r\bar c^a)
+
\bar\rho(c^a\partial_i\eta_r+\bar c^a\partial_i\bar\eta_r),
}
\label{eq:calc_Jr}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{r,i}^a
=
(c^a\partial_i\eta_r+\bar c^a\partial_i\bar\eta_r)\bar\chi.
}
\label{eq:calc_Kr}
\end{equation}
Thus
\[
(J_A,K_A),\qquad (J_E,K_E),\qquad (J_O,K_O)
\]
are explicit in terms of the orbit data \((N_r,\eta_r)\), the background \((\bar\rho,\bar\chi)\), and the internal coefficients \(c^a\).
:contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\section{3. Minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation}

In the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation one has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_r^a=0
\qquad
\forall r\in\{A,E,O\},
}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_A=K_E=K_O=0.
}
\label{eq:calc_Kzero}
\end{equation}
Therefore every fast six-row coefficient vanishes identically:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AA}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{OO}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AE}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AO}
=
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EO}
=
0.
}
\label{eq:calc_Hzero}
\end{equation}

Substituting into \eqref{eq:calc_Q2_numeric},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0.
}
\end{equation}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0
\qquad
\text{in the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation.}
}
\label{eq:calc_beta_zero}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7} :contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\section{4. What is the first nonzero source beyond the rigid truncation?}

Once \(K_A,K_E,K_O\) cease to vanish, the corrected odd coefficient is controlled by the weighted linear combination \eqref{eq:calc_Q2_numeric}. The absolute weights are:
\[
4.1472\times10^{-4},\qquad
2.7648\times10^{-4},\qquad
2.7648\times10^{-4},\qquad
9.216\times10^{-5},\qquad
4.608\times10^{-5},\qquad
4.608\times10^{-5}.
\]
Therefore the relative hierarchy is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|EE|:|AE|:|EO|:|AO|:|AA|:|OO|=9:6:6:2:1:1.
}
\label{eq:calc_weight_hierarchy}
\end{equation}

So if the six rows are of comparable microscopic size after the rigid truncation is lifted, then the leading corrected odd response is dominated first by
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE},
\]
next by
\[
H^{(2)}_{AE},\qquad H^{(2)}_{EO},
\]
and only then by
\[
H^{(2)}_{AO},\qquad H^{(2)}_{AA},\qquad H^{(2)}_{OO}.
\]

\section{5. Practical next computation order}

Therefore the correct source-by-source priority order is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(J_E,K_E)\ \text{first},
\qquad
(J_A,K_E)\ \text{and}\ (J_O,K_E)\ \text{next},
}
\end{equation}
equivalently
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE}\ \text{first},
\qquad
H^{(2)}_{AE},\ H^{(2)}_{EO}\ \text{second}.
}
\end{equation}

This is the first genuinely nonredundant microscopic direction beyond the rigid first-shell ansatz.

So the next actual microscopic calculation should start from the \(E\)-sector current pair \((J_E,K_E)\).
