\section{Actual Computation of the \(E\)-Sector Source for the First Nonzero Odd Transverse Response}

\section{Short explanation}

The six-row fast practical approximation is already explicit:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_rK_s^\dagger+J_sK_r^\dagger+K_rJ_s^\dagger+K_sJ_r^\dagger
\big].
}
\label{eq:Esrc_Hfast}
\end{equation}

The corrected odd transverse coefficient is then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0
\Bigl[
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{AA}
+
4.1472\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{EE}
+
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{OO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{AE}
+
9.216\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{AO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{EO}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:Esrc_beta_corr}
\end{equation}

Therefore the \(E\)-sector source \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\) is the single most heavily weighted fast coefficient in the odd corrected shift. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\section{1. Exact \(E\)-sector currents}

From the completed orbit-current formulas,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
N_E=\bar\Psi^\dagger\Phi_E+\Phi_E^\dagger\bar\Psi,
\qquad
M_E^a=\bar\Psi^\dagger T^a\Phi_E+\Phi_E^\dagger T^a\bar\Psi,
}
\label{eq:Esrc_NE_ME}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{E,i}^a=\partial_i M_E^a,
}
\label{eq:Esrc_JE_exact}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{E,i}^a
=
\partial_i\!\left[
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho}
\right]\bar\chi
+
(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E.
}
\label{eq:Esrc_KE_exact}
\end{equation}

It is convenient to define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
F_E^a
:=
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho}.
}
\label{eq:Esrc_FE_def}
\end{equation}
Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
K_{E,i}^a=(\partial_iF_E^a)\bar\chi+(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E.
}
\label{eq:Esrc_KE_FE}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\section{2. Exact fast formula for \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\)}

Set \(r=s=E\) in \eqref{eq:Esrc_Hfast}. Since all four terms coincide pairwise,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger
\big].
}
\label{eq:Esrc_HEE_pair}
\end{equation}

Substitute \eqref{eq:Esrc_JE_exact} and \eqref{eq:Esrc_KE_FE}:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_iM_E^a)\bigl((\partial_iF_E^a)\bar\chi+(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl((\partial_iF_E^a)\bar\chi+(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\bigr)(\partial_iM_E^a)^\dagger
\Big].
}
\label{eq:Esrc_HEE_expanded}
\end{equation}
The sums over \(i\) and \(a\) are implicit.

This is already the exact closed \(E\)-sector formula needed for the fast practical audit.

\section{3. Source decomposition of \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\)}

Equation \eqref{eq:Esrc_HEE_expanded} splits naturally into two parts:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
+
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}},
}
\label{eq:Esrc_HEE_split}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_iM_E^a)\bigl((\partial_iF_E^a)\bar\chi\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl((\partial_iF_E^a)\bar\chi\bigr)(\partial_iM_E^a)^\dagger
\Big],
}
\label{eq:Esrc_HEE_proj}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_iM_E^a)\bigl((\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl((\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\bigr)(\partial_iM_E^a)^\dagger
\Big].
}
\label{eq:Esrc_HEE_qgrad}
\end{equation}

Thus the first nonzero odd transverse response can arise from either

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_iF_E^a\neq 0
\quad\text{(projector/internal texture source)}
}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_i\bar q^a\neq 0
\quad\text{(background charge-gradient source).}
}
\end{equation}

\section{4. Further explicit expansion of the projector/internal texture source}

Differentiate \eqref{eq:Esrc_FE_def}:
\begin{align}
\partial_iF_E^a
&=
\partial_i\!\left(\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho}\right)
\nonumber\\
&=
\frac{
\partial_iM_E^a-(\partial_i\bar q^a)N_E-\bar q^a\partial_iN_E
}{\bar\rho}
-
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho^2}\,\partial_i\bar\rho.
\end{align}
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_iF_E^a
=
\frac{\partial_iM_E^a-\bar q^a\partial_iN_E}{\bar\rho}
-
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho^2}\,\partial_i\bar\rho
-
\frac{(\partial_i\bar q^a)N_E}{\bar\rho}.
}
\label{eq:Esrc_dFE_full}
\end{equation}

So the projector/internal-texture contribution already contains three distinct microscopic slots:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_iM_E^a
\quad\text{(orbit-current gradient),}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar q^a\partial_iN_E,\ (M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E)\partial_i\bar\rho
\quad\text{(density-modulated projector source),}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(\partial_i\bar q^a)N_E
\quad\text{(charge-gradient leakage into the projector channel).}
}
\end{equation}

Thus \(H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}\) is already a sum of several microscopic non-rigid mechanisms.

\section{5. Rigid truncation check}

In the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation, the notes prove
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_r^a=0,\qquad K_A=K_E=K_O=0.
}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\[
F_E^a=0,\qquad
\partial_iF_E^a=0,\qquad
\partial_i\bar q^a=0.
\]
Therefore both source pieces vanish:
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}=0,
\qquad
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}=0.
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}=0
\qquad
\text{in the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation.}
}
\label{eq:Esrc_HEE_rigid_zero}
\end{equation}

This reproduces the previously established result that
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0
\]
in that truncation. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\section{6. First nonzero criterion for \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\)}

From \eqref{eq:Esrc_HEE_split}, a sufficient criterion for the first odd source to be nonzero is:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_iM_E^a)\bigl((\partial_iF_E^a)\bar\chi\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl((\partial_iF_E^a)\bar\chi\bigr)(\partial_iM_E^a)^\dagger
\Big]\neq 0
}
\end{equation}
or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_iM_E^a)\bigl((\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl((\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\bigr)(\partial_iM_E^a)^\dagger
\Big]\neq 0.
}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the three minimal requirements are:

\begin{enumerate}
\item \(K_E\neq 0\), i.e. some non-rigid internal/projector or charge-gradient structure must exist;
\item the resulting \(J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger\) must carry a nonzero \(\Sigma_2\) component;
\item that \(\Sigma_2\) component must survive the odd projector \(\mathfrak P_O\).
\end{enumerate}

So the real obstruction is not the absence of a formula.
It is whether the frozen corrected branch contains a genuinely odd-projectable phase-resolved \(E\)-sector mixed current.

\section{7. Dominant contribution to \(\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}\)}

Since the corrected odd shift is
\[
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0\,
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}}),
\]
and the largest weight in \(Q_2\) is the \(EE\)-entry,
\[
4.1472\times 10^{-4},
\]
the first nonzero \(\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}\) beyond the rigid truncation is dominated, unless strong cancellations occur, by
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE}.
}
\end{equation}

More precisely, if
\[
|H^{(2)}_{EE}|
\gg
\max\left\{
\frac{2.7648}{4.1472}|H^{(2)}_{AE}|,
\frac{2.7648}{4.1472}|H^{(2)}_{EO}|,
\frac{0.9216}{4.1472}|H^{(2)}_{AO}|,
\frac{0.4608}{4.1472}|H^{(2)}_{AA}|,
\frac{0.4608}{4.1472}|H^{(2)}_{OO}|
\right\},
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0
\left(4.1472\times10^{-4}\right)H^{(2)}_{EE}.
}
\label{eq:Esrc_beta_dominant}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:Esrc_HEE_split}, this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0
\left(4.1472\times10^{-4}\right)
\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\Bigl[
\mathfrak P_O(\cdots)_{\mathrm{proj}}
+
\mathfrak P_O(\cdots)_{\mathrm{qgrad}}
\Bigr].
}
\end{equation}

So the sign and size of the first odd transverse activation are controlled directly by the odd-projected Hermitian mixed current in the \(E\)-sector.

\section{Final summary}

The exact fast \(E\)-sector coefficient is
\[
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger
\big],
\]
with
\[
J_{E,i}^a=\partial_iM_E^a,
\qquad
K_{E,i}^a
=
\partial_i\!\left[
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho}
\right]\bar\chi
+
(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E.
\]

Therefore the first nonzero odd source splits exactly into
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
\quad+\quad
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}},
\]
namely projector/internal texture and background charge-gradient contributions.

In the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation,
\[
F_E^a=0,\qquad \partial_iF_E^a=0,\qquad \partial_i\bar q^a=0,
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}=0,
\qquad
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0.
}
\]

Beyond that rigid truncation, the first nonzero odd transverse activation is controlled first by the odd-projectable \(E\)-sector mixed current \(J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger\).

\section{Final summary}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Current stage: actual computation of the leading }E\text{-sector odd transverse source.}
}
\end{equation}

The exact \(E\)-sector orbit-current pair is
\[
J_{E,i}^a=\partial_iM_E^a,
\qquad
K_{E,i}^a
=
\partial_i\!\left[
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho}
\right]\bar\chi
+
(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E.
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

Hence the fast six-row coefficient is
\[
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger
\big].
\]

This splits exactly into
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
\quad+\quad
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}},
\]
where the first comes from
\[
\partial_i\!\left[
\frac{M_E^a-\bar q^aN_E}{\bar\rho}
\right]\bar\chi
\]
and the second from
\[
(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E.
\]

Therefore the first nonzero odd transverse source beyond the rigid truncation can come from either:

\[
\boxed{
\partial_iF_E^a\neq0
\quad\text{(non-rigid internal/projector texture),}
}
\]
or
\[
\boxed{
\partial_i\bar q^a\neq0
\quad\text{(background charge-gradient source).}
}
\]

In the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation,
\[
F_E^a=0,\qquad \partial_iF_E^a=0,\qquad \partial_i\bar q^a=0,
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}=0,
\qquad
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0.
}
\]
:contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

Since the largest weight in the corrected odd shift
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})
\]
sits in front of \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\), the \(E\)-sector remains the first decisive microscopic test for whether \(\Lambda_O\neq0\) beyond the rigid truncation. :contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Goal C: evaluate }\partial_iF_E^a\text{ and }\partial_i\bar q^a\text{ on the frozen corrected branch.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Goal M: decide whether }H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}\text{ or }H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}\text{ is the first nonzero odd source.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Goal S: once }H^{(2)}_{EE}\neq0\text{ is confirmed, use it as the leading source for }\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}.
}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual Decision Between the Two \(E\)-Sector Sources: \texorpdfstring{$\partial_iF_E^a$}{dF} versus \texorpdfstring{$\partial_i\bar q^a$}{dq}}

\section{Short explanation}

The completed orbit-current formulas are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{r,i}^a=\partial_iM_r^a,
\qquad
K_{r,i}^a=(\partial_iQ_r^a)\bar\chi+(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_r,
}
\label{eq:src_choice_JK}
\end{equation}
with
\[
Q_r^a=\frac{M_r^a-\bar q^aN_r}{\bar\rho}.
\]

Therefore the fast \(E\)-sector coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger
\big].
}
\label{eq:src_choice_HEE}
\end{equation}

The question is: which part of
\[
K_E=(\partial_iQ_E^a)\bar\chi+(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E
\]
is the first unavoidable nonzero source on the frozen corrected branch?

\section{1. Exact split of \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\)}

Substitute \eqref{eq:src_choice_JK} into \eqref{eq:src_choice_HEE}:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
+
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}},
}
\end{equation}
where
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_iM_E^a)\bigl((\partial_iQ_E^a)\bar\chi\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl((\partial_iQ_E^a)\bar\chi\bigr)(\partial_iM_E^a)^\dagger
\Big],
}
\label{eq:src_choice_proj}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_iM_E^a)\bigl((\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl((\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\bigr)(\partial_iM_E^a)^\dagger
\Big].
}
\label{eq:src_choice_qgrad}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Rigid truncation check}

In the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation one has
\[
Q_E^a=0,
\qquad
\partial_iP=0,
\qquad
\partial_i\bar q^a=0.
\]
Hence both pieces vanish:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}=0,
\qquad
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}=0,
\qquad
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}=0.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})=0,
\qquad
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0
\]
in that truncation.

\section{3. Defect-background evaluation of \(\partial_i\bar q^a\)}

For the locked one-defect background
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Psi_B(\xi,x_\parallel)=\phi_0(x_\parallel)\,z_B(\xi),
\qquad
\bar\rho=|\phi_0|^2,
}
\end{equation}
the background charge density is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bar q^a
=
\frac{\bar\Psi^\dagger T^a\bar\Psi}{\bar\rho}
=
z_B^\dagger T^a z_B
=:m_a(\theta).
}
\label{eq:src_choice_qbar}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_i\bar q^a
=
\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\,\partial_\theta m_a(\theta).
}
\label{eq:src_choice_dqbar}
\end{equation}

So on a genuine defect background, the q-gradient source is automatically present unless
\[
\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\equiv0
\]
for the relevant internal component.

\section{4. Explicit q-gradient formula for the first unavoidable source}

Substituting \eqref{eq:src_choice_dqbar} into \eqref{eq:src_choice_qgrad}, only the \(\xi\)-component survives:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\bigl(\theta'(\xi)\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\,\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl(\theta'(\xi)\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\,\chi_E\bigr)(\partial_\xi M_E^a)^\dagger
\Big].
}
\label{eq:src_choice_HEE_qgrad_explicit}
\end{equation}

This is the first unavoidable odd-source formula beyond the rigid truncation.

\section{5. Why the q-gradient source is the first generic candidate}

The projector/internal-texture contribution \(H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}\) requires
\[
\partial_iQ_E^a\neq0,
\]
which in turn needs a non-rigid projector/internal completion beyond the locked first-shell orbit ansatz.

By contrast, the q-gradient piece requires only:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\theta'(\xi)\not\equiv0,
\qquad
\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\not\equiv0,
}
\end{equation}
which are already natural on a genuine one-defect background.

Therefore the first generic candidate for a nonzero \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\) on the frozen corrected branch is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}},
}
\end{equation}
while
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
\]
is the first optional completion-level correction.

\section{6. Necessary and sufficient odd-projection condition}

A nonzero q-gradient source still requires survival of the odd projector.
From \eqref{eq:src_choice_HEE_qgrad_explicit}, the exact condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\chi_E^\dagger+\chi_E(\partial_\xi M_E^a)^\dagger
\Big]
\neq 0
}
\label{eq:src_choice_PO_condition}
\end{equation}
on a set of nonzero \(\xi\)-measure where
\[
\theta'(\xi)\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\neq0.
\]

So the first nonzero odd transverse activation is controlled by:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the defect profile gradient \(\theta'(\xi)\),
\item the internal rotation rate \(\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\),
\item the odd-projected phase-resolved overlap between \(\partial_\xi M_E^a\) and \(\chi_E\).
\end{enumerate}

\section{7. Dominant corrected odd shift}

Because the corrected odd shift uses
\[
Q_2(\delta_{\mathrm{corr}})
=
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{AA}
+
4.1472\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{EE}
+
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{OO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{AE}
+
9.216\times10^{-5}H^{(2)}_{AO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2)}_{EO},
\]
the \(EE\)-slot is the most heavily weighted one.

Hence, once \eqref{eq:src_choice_PO_condition} is satisfied and no large cancellation occurs, the leading corrected odd coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0
\left(4.1472\times10^{-4}\right)
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
}
\label{eq:src_choice_beta_leading}
\end{equation}

\section{Final summary}

The exact \(E\)-sector odd source is
\[
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
+
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
\]

The projector/internal-texture piece is
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
\propto
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_iM_E^a)\bigl((\partial_iQ_E^a)\bar\chi\bigr)^\dagger
+\mathrm{h.c.}
\Big],
\]
while the q-gradient piece is
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
\propto
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\bigl(\theta'(\xi)\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+\mathrm{h.c.}
\Big].
\]

In the rigid first-shell truncation both vanish, so
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE}=0,\qquad \beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0.
\]

Beyond that truncation, the first generic candidate is the q-gradient source, because it is already carried by the genuine defect background.
Therefore the first decisive microscopic test is:
\[
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\chi_E^\dagger+\chi_E(\partial_\xi M_E^a)^\dagger
\Big]\stackrel{?}{\neq}0.
}
\]

\section{Final summary}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Current stage: first actual decision between the two }E\text{-sector odd sources.}
}
\end{equation}

The exact completed orbit-current formulas are
\[
J_{E,i}^a=\partial_iM_E^a,
\qquad
K_{E,i}^a=(\partial_iQ_E^a)\bar\chi+(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E.
\]
So
\[
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger
\big]
\]
splits exactly into
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
\quad+\quad
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
\]

For the defect background
\[
\bar q^a=z_B^\dagger T^a z_B=:m_a(\theta),
\]
one has
\[
\partial_i\bar q^a=\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)\partial_\theta m_a(\theta).
\]

Therefore the first unavoidable post-rigid source is
\[
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\bigl(\theta'(\xi)\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+\mathrm{h.c.}
\Big].
}
\]

In the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation,
\[
Q_E^a=0,\qquad \partial_i\bar q^a=0,
\]
so
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE}=0,\qquad \beta^{\mathrm{corr}}=0.
\]

Hence the first generic candidate for \(\Lambda_O\neq0\) beyond the rigid truncation is not the projector/internal-texture source but the background q-gradient source.

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Goal C: evaluate }\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)\text{ and the odd-projected overlap }
\mathfrak P_O[(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\chi_E^\dagger+\chi_E(\partial_\xi M_E^a)^\dagger].
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Goal M: decide whether }H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}\neq0\text{ already on the frozen corrected branch.}
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Goal S: if yes, use }H^{(2)}_{EE}\text{ as the leading source for }\beta^{\mathrm{corr}};\text{ if not, move to }H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}.
}
\end{equation}

%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%%

\section{Actual Computation: the \(q\)-Gradient Source is the First Generic Odd Transverse Activation}

\section{Short explanation}

The completed \(E\)-sector currents are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{E,i}^a=\partial_i M_E^a,
\qquad
K_{E,i}^a=(\partial_iQ_E^a)\bar\chi+(\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E.
}
\label{eq:qgrad_JK_E}
\end{equation}

Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\big[
J_EK_E^\dagger+K_EJ_E^\dagger
\big]
=
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}+H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
}
\label{eq:qgrad_HEE_split}
\end{equation}

We now show that, on the explicit embedded \(SU(2)_{(13)}\) defect branch, the \(q\)-gradient source is the first generic nonzero candidate beyond the rigid truncation.

\section{1. Explicit defect branch data}

Take the embedded \(SU(2)_{(13)}\) generators
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_1=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&1\\
0&0&0\\
1&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\quad
T_2=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&0&-i\\
0&0&0\\
i&0&0
\end{pmatrix},
\quad
T_3=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
1&0&0\\
0&0&0\\
0&0&-1
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

Take the real defect representative
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
z_B(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
\cos\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\sin\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
e_1(\xi)=
\begin{pmatrix}
-\sin\theta(\xi)\\
0\\
\cos\theta(\xi)
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

Define
\[
m_a(\theta):=z_B^\dagger T_a z_B,
\qquad
k_a(\theta):=\Tr\!\Big[T_a(e_1z_B^\dagger+z_Be_1^\dagger)\Big],
\qquad
A_a(\theta):=e_1^\dagger T_a z_B+z_B^\dagger T_a e_1.
\]

Direct evaluation gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m_1=\frac12\sin2\theta,
\qquad
m_2=0,
\qquad
m_3=\frac12\cos2\theta,
}
\label{eq:qgrad_m}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
k_1=\cos2\theta,
\qquad
k_2=0,
\qquad
k_3=-\sin2\theta,
}
\label{eq:qgrad_k}
\end{equation}
and
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_a(\theta)=k_a(\theta).
}
\label{eq:qgrad_Aeqk}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\section{2. Exact derivative identity}

Differentiate \eqref{eq:qgrad_m} with respect to \(\theta\):
\[
\partial_\theta m_1=\cos2\theta,\qquad
\partial_\theta m_2=0,\qquad
\partial_\theta m_3=-\sin2\theta.
\]
Comparing with \eqref{eq:qgrad_k}, we obtain the exact identity
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)=k_a(\theta)=A_a(\theta).
}
\label{eq:qgrad_dm_eq_k}
\end{equation}

Now on the defect background
\[
\bar q^a=z_B^\dagger T_a z_B=m_a(\theta),
\]
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_i\bar q^a
=
\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\,\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)
=
\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta).
}
\label{eq:qgrad_dq_exact}
\end{equation}

This is the key exact computation: the \(q\)-gradient source is aligned with the tangent adjoint vector \(k_a\).

\section{3. Explicit q-gradient contribution to \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\)}

Substitute \eqref{eq:qgrad_dq_exact} into the \(q\)-gradient piece:
\begin{equation}
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_iM_E^a)\bigl((\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl((\partial_i\bar q^a)\chi_E\bigr)(\partial_iM_E^a)^\dagger
\Big].
\end{equation}

Only the normal component survives, so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\bigl(\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl(\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\chi_E\bigr)(\partial_\xi M_E^a)^\dagger
\Big].
}
\label{eq:qgrad_HEE_final}
\end{equation}

Using \(A_a=k_a\), one may also write
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\bigl(\theta'(\xi)A_a(\theta)\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl(\theta'(\xi)A_a(\theta)\chi_E\bigr)(\partial_\xi M_E^a)^\dagger
\Big].
}
\end{equation}

Thus the first generic odd source is carried by the same tangent internal direction that already appeared in the branch geometry.

\section{4. Parity check}

For the reflection-symmetric defect profile,
\[
\theta(-\xi)=\theta(\xi),
\]
one has
\[
\theta'(-\xi)=-\theta'(\xi).
\]
Since \(m_a(\theta)\), \(k_a(\theta)\), and \(A_a(\theta)\) are functions of \(\theta\) only, they are even in \(\xi\).
Therefore
\[
\partial_i\bar q^a
=
\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)
\]
is odd in \(\xi\).

This matches the general odd-kernel requirement for the transport operator built from defect gradients.
So the q-gradient source is not parity-forbidden. :contentReference[oaicite:3]{index=3}

\section{5. Why the projector/internal source is subleading generically}

The projector/internal source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_iM_E^a)\bigl((\partial_iQ_E^a)\bar\chi\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl((\partial_iQ_E^a)\bar\chi\bigr)(\partial_iM_E^a)^\dagger
\Big].
}
\label{eq:qgrad_HEE_proj}
\end{equation}

This requires
\[
\partial_iQ_E^a\neq0,
\]
which is absent in the minimal rigid-internal first-shell truncation and only appears after a non-rigid projector/internal completion.

By contrast, the q-gradient piece requires only
\[
\theta'(\xi)\not\equiv0
\quad\text{and}\quad
k_a(\theta)\not\equiv0,
\]
both of which are already present on the genuine defect background.

Therefore the first generic candidate beyond the rigid truncation is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}},
}
\end{equation}
not \(H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}\).

\section{6. Explicit nonzero criterion}

From \eqref{eq:qgrad_HEE_final}, a sufficient condition for a nonzero odd \(E\)-sector source is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)(k_a\chi_E)^\dagger
+
(k_a\chi_E)(\partial_\xi M_E^a)^\dagger
\Big]
\neq0
}
\label{eq:qgrad_nonzero_criterion}
\end{equation}
on a set of nonzero \(\xi\)-measure where \(\theta'(\xi)\neq0\).

Because the corrected odd shift weights \(H^{(2)}_{EE}\) most strongly, once \eqref{eq:qgrad_nonzero_criterion} holds and no accidental cancellation occurs, the leading corrected odd coefficient is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0
\left(4.1472\times10^{-4}\right)
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{7. Final theorem}

\begin{theorem}[First generic odd source on the frozen corrected branch]
On the embedded \(SU(2)_{(13)}\) defect branch one has
\[
\partial_\theta m_a(\theta)=k_a(\theta)=A_a(\theta),
\]
hence
\[
\partial_i\bar q^a=\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta).
\]

Therefore, beyond the rigid first-shell truncation, the first generic candidate for a nonzero odd transverse response in the dominant \(E\)-sector slot is
\[
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}},
\]
not \(H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{proj}}\).

A sufficient condition for activation is
\[
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)(k_a\chi_E)^\dagger
+
(k_a\chi_E)(\partial_\xi M_E^a)^\dagger
\Big]\neq0
\]
on a region where \(\theta'(\xi)\neq0\).
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The derivative identity follows by direct differentiation of the explicit \(m_a(\theta)\).
Substituting it into the completed \(E\)-sector current formula gives the explicit q-gradient source.
The projector/internal source requires an additional non-rigid completion \(\partial_iQ_E^a\neq0\), whereas the q-gradient source is already carried by the defect background itself.
\end{proof}

\section{Final summary}

The exact embedded defect branch satisfies
\[
m_1=\frac12\sin2\theta,\quad m_2=0,\quad m_3=\frac12\cos2\theta,
\]
\[
k_1=\cos2\theta,\quad k_2=0,\quad k_3=-\sin2\theta,
\]
so
\[
\boxed{
\partial_\theta m_a=k_a=A_a.
}
\]

Hence on the defect background
\[
\boxed{
\partial_i\bar q^a=\delta_{i\xi}\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta),
}
\]
and the dominant \(E\)-sector odd source becomes
\[
\boxed{
H^{(2)}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\Big[
(\partial_\xi M_E^a)\bigl(\theta'k_a\chi_E\bigr)^\dagger
+
\bigl(\theta'k_a\chi_E\bigr)(\partial_\xi M_E^a)^\dagger
\Big].
}
\]

Therefore the first generic nonzero source beyond the rigid truncation is the q-gradient source, not the projector/internal one.

\end{equation}

So beyond the rigid truncation, the first generic nonzero candidate is the q-gradient source, not the projector/internal source.

\section{Actual Fourier-Shell Formula for the First Generic Odd Source}

\section{Short explanation}

At this point the only genuinely missing ingredient is not a new theorem.
It is the finite harmonic overlap evaluation on the frozen corrected branch.

The completed Fourier-space orbit currents are already explicit:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat M_r^a(Q)
=
\sum_G
\Bigl(
\bar A_G^\dagger T^a B_{G+Q}^{(r)}
+
B_G^{(r)\dagger}T^a\bar A_{G+Q}
\Bigr),
}
\label{eq:FS_Mhat}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat J_{r,i}^a(Q)=iQ_i\,\widehat M_r^a(Q),
}
\label{eq:FS_Jhat}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widehat K_{r,i}^a(Q)
=
iQ_i\,\widehat Q_r^a(Q)\,\bar\chi
+
(\partial_i\bar q^a)\widehat\chi_r(Q).
}
\label{eq:FS_Khat}
\end{equation}
So the remaining odd-source audit is a literal finite overlap computation. :contentReference[oaicite:2]{index=2}

\section{1. Exact \(E\)-sector q-gradient contribution in Fourier space}

The fast six-row coefficient is
\begin{equation}
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{rs}
=
-\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\sum_Q \widehat J_{r,i}^a(Q)\widehat K_{s,i}^a(-Q)^\dagger
+
\sum_Q \widehat J_{s,i}^a(Q)\widehat K_{r,i}^a(-Q)^\dagger
+\mathrm{h.c.}
\right].
\label{eq:FS_Hfast}
\end{equation}

For the \(E\)-sector q-gradient source, keep only the \((\partial_i\bar q^a)\widehat\chi_E\) term in \(\widehat K_E\) and set \(r=s=E\). Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\sum_Q
\widehat J_{E,i}^a(Q)
\bigl((\partial_i\bar q^a)\widehat\chi_E(-Q)\bigr)^\dagger
+\mathrm{h.c.}
\right].
}
\label{eq:FS_HEE_qgrad_start}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:FS_Jhat},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\sum_Q
iQ_i\,\widehat M_E^a(Q)
\bigl((\partial_i\bar q^a)\widehat\chi_E(-Q)\bigr)^\dagger
+\mathrm{h.c.}
\right].
}
\label{eq:FS_HEE_qgrad_Mchi}
\end{equation}

\section{2. Defect-background specialization}

On the embedded one-defect background,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\partial_i\bar q^a
=
\delta_{i\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)\,k_a(\theta).
}
\label{eq:FS_dqbar}
\end{equation}

Therefore only the normal component survives:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
-\frac{2\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\sum_Q
iQ_\xi\,\widehat M_E^a(Q)
\bigl(\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\widehat\chi_E(-Q)\bigr)^\dagger
+\mathrm{h.c.}
\right].
}
\label{eq:FS_HEE_qgrad_xi}
\end{equation}

Assume the background gauge is chosen so that \(\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\) is real.
Then for each \(Q\),
\[
iQ_\xi\,\widehat M_E^a(Q)\bigl(\theta'k_a\widehat\chi_E(-Q)\bigr)^\dagger+\mathrm{h.c.}
=
-2Q_\xi\,\theta'k_a\,\Im\!\Bigl(\widehat M_E^a(Q)\overline{\widehat\chi_E(-Q)}\Bigr).
\]
Hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
=
\frac{4\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\sum_Q
Q_\xi\,\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\,
\Im\!\Bigl(\widehat M_E^a(Q)\overline{\widehat\chi_E(-Q)}\Bigr)
\right].
}
\label{eq:FS_HEE_qgrad_im}
\end{equation}

This is the first genuine finite shell-overlap formula for the odd source.

\section{3. Exact nonzero criterion}

Equation \eqref{eq:FS_HEE_qgrad_im} shows that a sufficient condition for a nonzero odd \(E\)-sector source is the existence of at least one shell momentum \(Q\) such that
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q_\xi\neq 0,
\qquad
\Im\!\Bigl(\widehat M_E^a(Q)\overline{\widehat\chi_E(-Q)}\Bigr)\neq 0,
\qquad
\mathfrak P_O\text{ does not kill the corresponding component.}
}
\label{eq:FS_nonzero_criterion}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, the first generic odd transverse activation requires:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a shell harmonic with nonzero normal momentum component;
\item a genuine phase misalignment between the \(E\)-sector orbit current \(\widehat M_E^a(Q)\) and the worldvolume derivative mode \(\widehat\chi_E(Q)\);
\item survival of that component under the odd projector.
\end{enumerate}

Thus the first generic source is not an arbitrary background scalar.
It is the odd-projected \emph{imaginary shell overlap} between the \(E\)-sector current and the \(E\)-sector test-mode derivative.

\section{4. Dominant first-shell approximation}

If the frozen corrected branch is sharply peaked on the selected first shell and the dominant contribution comes from the two opposite selected shell modes \(Q=\pm G_*\), then using the reality relations
\[
\widehat M_E^a(-G_*)=\overline{\widehat M_E^a(G_*)},
\qquad
\widehat\chi_E(-G_*)=\overline{\widehat\chi_E(G_*)},
\]
the two terms combine and give
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}
\approx
\frac{8\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
G_{*\xi}\,\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\,
\Im\!\Bigl(\widehat M_E^a(G_*)\overline{\widehat\chi_E(G_*)}\Bigr)
\right].
}
\label{eq:FS_HEE_qgrad_firstshell}
\end{equation}

So in the first-shell-dominant regime, the whole problem collapses to a \emph{single shell-phase overlap test}.

\section{5. Leading corrected odd coefficient}

The corrected odd shift is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0
\Bigl[
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AA}
+
4.1472\times10^{-4}H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE}
+
4.608\times10^{-5}H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{OO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AE}
+
9.216\times10^{-5}H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{AO}
-
2.7648\times10^{-4}H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EO}
\Bigr].
}
\label{eq:FS_beta_corr_again}
\end{equation}

Since the \(EE\)-slot has the largest weight, once \eqref{eq:FS_nonzero_criterion} holds and no accidental cancellation occurs,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa\,A_0
\left(4.1472\times10^{-4}\right)
H^{(2),\mathrm{fast}}_{EE,\mathrm{qgrad}}.
}
\label{eq:FS_beta_dominant}
\end{equation}

Substituting \eqref{eq:FS_HEE_qgrad_im},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta^{\mathrm{corr}}
\approx
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{4}\,
\frac{\alpha_X\beta_X}{M_X^2}\,
\theta_0\kappa\,A_0\,
\left(4.1472\times10^{-4}\right)\,
\mathfrak P_O\!\left[
\sum_Q
Q_\xi\,\theta'(\xi)k_a(\theta)\,
\Im\!\Bigl(\widehat M_E^a(Q)\overline{\widehat\chi_E(-Q)}\Bigr)
\right].
}
\label{eq:FS_beta_final_explicit}
\end{equation}

\section{6. What is computed and what remains}

What is now computed exactly:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the first generic odd source is the }E\text{-sector }q\text{-gradient shell overlap}

\end{equation}
and its exact finite formula is \eqref{eq:FS_HEE_qgrad_im}.

What remains is a literal finite harmonic evaluation:

into

\]
and test whether
\[
\Im\!\Bigl(\widehat M_E^a(Q)\overline{\widehat\chi_E(-Q)}\Bigr)
\]
survives the odd projector.

\section{Immediate Forward Route: Explicit Odd Extra Carrier Instead of the Unavailable Frozen-Harmonic JK Audit}

\section{Short explanation}

The \(JK\)-route q-gradient audit has been reduced as far as possible using the currently available files.

which requires the actual frozen-branch harmonics
\[

These harmonics are not numerically or symbolically instantiated in the present conversation context. :contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4} :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

So the correct non-stalling move is to switch to the already explicit lowest-order complete realization route, where the odd transverse carrier is fully written and directly nonzero on the defect background. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\section{1. Explicit odd extra carrier}

On the embedded \(SU(2)_{(13)}\) defect branch, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_O:=i(e_2z_B^\dagger-z_Be_2^\dagger),
}
\end{equation}
and the odd generator
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_O:=\frac12
\begin{pmatrix}
0&-i&0\\
i&0&0\\
0&0&0
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
q_O(\theta):=\Tr(S_O M_O)=\cos\theta.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore the explicit odd extra slot is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
=
X_i^{(O)}\,\Tr(S_O M_O)\,J_jD_j\psi
=
X_i^{(O)}\,\cos\theta(\xi)\,J_jD_j\psi.
}
\label{eq:IO_explicit_final}
\end{equation}

So whenever
\[
\cos\theta\not\equiv 0,
\]
the odd extra carrier is locally nonzero. :contentReference[oaicite:7]{index=7}

\section{2. Induced tangent transport block}

The induced tangent transport block from the explicit extra \(E/O\) slots is

\end{equation}

Thus the odd transport density is explicitly present at lowest order:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_O^{(EO)}\neq 0
\quad\text{whenever}\quad
\widetilde\Lambda_O\neq0,\ 
\theta'(\xi)\not\equiv0,\ 
\cos\theta(\xi)\not\equiv0.

:contentReference[oaicite:8]{index=8}

\section{1. Projection to the Bloch zero modes}

Let \(u_a^\pm(\xi)=f_\pm(\xi)e_a(\xi)\) be the opposite-valley low modes.

e_b(\xi).
}
\label{eq:EO_insert_projection}
\end{equation}

Define the overlap integrals
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_3:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
I_c:=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi).
}
\label{eq:EO_insert_overlap}
\end{equation}

Then the reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c,
\qquad
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c.
}
\label{eq:EO_insert_reducedcoeffs}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, with the notation \(I_{\theta,\cos}\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha=\widetilde\Lambda_E I_{\theta,\cos},
\qquad
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_{\theta,\cos}.
}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:9]{index=9} :contentReference[oaicite:10]{index=10} :contentReference[oaicite:11]{index=11}

\section{2. Explicit reduced PDE}

Therefore the solved lowest-order Branch-B reduced PDE becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Bigl[
i\partial_t
-
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3\,\sigma_3(-i\partial_\parallel)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_E\bigl(\sigma_1(-i\partial_1)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_2)\bigr)
-
I_c\widetilde\Lambda_O\bigl(-\sigma_1(-i\partial_2)+\sigma_2(-i\partial_1)\bigr)
\Bigr]\chi=0.
}
\label{eq:EO_insert_finalPDE}
\end{equation}

Thus the odd transverse coefficient is not schematic anymore.
It is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c.
}
\label{eq:EO_insert_beta}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:12]{index=12} :contentReference[oaicite:13]{index=13}

\section{3. Minimal nonzero condition for the odd channel}

From \eqref{eq:EO_insert_beta}, the odd transverse channel is nonzero if and only if
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
I_c\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:EO_insert_nonzero}
\end{equation}

Here
\[
I_c=\int d\xi\,f_+f_-\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\]
is the geometric overlap.
So the odd channel requires:

\begin{enumerate}
\item a nonzero microscopic odd transverse carrier coefficient \(\widetilde\Lambda_O\),
\item a nonvanishing defect/zero-mode overlap \(I_c\).
\end{enumerate}

This is the exact branch-level odd-channel reading.

\section{4. Relation to the source table}

At principal order, the source table is:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_3^{(\mathrm{prim})}=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}\theta'(\xi)^3,
\qquad
a_3^{(K)}=0,
\qquad
a_3^{(EO)}=0.
}
\end{equation}

So the longitudinal source is uniquely primitive, while both \(K\)-sector and \(EO\)-slot are purely transverse.
Therefore the odd channel does not compete with the longitudinal one; it simply enters the transverse reduced coefficient sheet through \(\widetilde\Lambda_O\). :contentReference[oaicite:14]{index=14} :contentReference[oaicite:15]{index=15} :contentReference[oaicite:16]{index=16}

\section{5. Exact branch-level deliverable}

The exact current deliverable is now:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_3,
\qquad
\alpha=\widetilde\Lambda_E I_c,
\qquad
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c.
}
\label{eq:EO_insert_deliverable}
\end{equation}

So the actual microscopic frontier is reduced to determining the coefficient point
\[
\lambda_c,\qquad \widetilde\Lambda_E,\qquad \widetilde\Lambda_O,
\]
with the odd channel already read explicitly through \(\widetilde\Lambda_O\).

\section{6. Honest current status}

What is now genuinely closed is the branch-level coefficient reading of the explicit odd carrier:
\[
\boxed{
\mathcal I_O
\Longrightarrow
b_O(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\Longrightarrow
\beta=\widetilde\Lambda_O I_c.
}
\]

What is still open is not the reduced reading itself, but the actual microscopic value/sign of
\[
\widetilde\Lambda_O.
\]
That is the remaining coefficient problem.

\section{Final summary}

The explicit extra odd carrier route is now fully inserted into the reduced coefficient sheet.

Its local transport density is
\[
b_O(\xi)=\widetilde\Lambda_O\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi),
\]
and after Bloch zero-mode projection the reduced odd transverse coefficient is
\[
\boxed{

\qquad

}

Therefore the odd transverse channel is nonzero exactly when
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O\neq 0
\quad\text{and}\quad
I_c\neq 0.
}
\]

This is the first fully explicit branch-level odd-channel formula available on the present data.

\section{Final summary}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Current stage: the explicit odd extra carrier has now been fully inserted into the reduced coefficient sheet.}

\end{equation}

The explicit \(EO\)-slot tangent transport block is

\section{Actual Reading of the Odd Coefficient on the Explicit Extra-Carrier Route}

\section{Goal}

The local odd carrier has already been identified explicitly.
The remaining task is to read its reduced coefficient and decide whether the present explicit branch can actually activate the odd channel.

\section{Exact reduced coefficient sheet}

For the solved lowest-order Branch-B realization, the reduced symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3}p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel=\frac{\lambda_c}{2}I_{\theta'^3},
\qquad
\alpha=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_E,
\qquad
\beta=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\label{eq:odd_reading_dictionary}
\end{equation}

\section{Microscopic one-mediator coefficient point}

At operator level, the one-mediator coefficient audit gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1.
}
\label{eq:odd_reading_operator}
\end{equation}

If the shell basis is canonically normalized so that
\[
C_\parallel=C_E=C_O=1,
\]
then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1.
}
\label{eq:odd_reading_canonical_operator}
\end{equation}

In the transport-side canonical explicit branch notation, the same normalization layer is absorbed into the coefficient point, so one writes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O^{(1)}
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:odd_reading_canonical_transport}
\end{equation}

\section{Explicit odd coefficient}

Substituting \eqref{eq:odd_reading_operator} into \eqref{eq:odd_reading_dictionary},
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_{\theta,\cos}.
}
\label{eq:odd_reading_beta_general}
\end{equation}

In the canonical explicit normalization this reduces to
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_{\theta,\cos}
}
\label{eq:odd_reading_beta_canonical}
\end{equation}
if the transport-side normalization absorbs \(J_1\), or
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,J_1\,I_{\theta,\cos}
}
\label{eq:odd_reading_beta_canonical_unabsorbed}
\end{equation}
if \(J_1\) is kept explicit.

\section{Minimal nonzero criterion}

Since
\[
I_{\theta,\cos}
=
\int d\xi\,f_+(\xi)f_-(\xi)\,\theta'(\xi)\cos\theta(\xi)
\]
is generically nonzero for a monotone defect profile with nontrivial \(\theta\)-variation and nonvanishing even--odd overlap,
the odd channel is nonzero exactly when
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta_X\neq 0,
\qquad
\gamma_O\neq 0,
\qquad
I_{\theta,\cos}\neq 0,
}
\label{eq:odd_reading_nonzero_min}
\end{equation}
and, in the unabsorbed operator normalization,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
C_OJ_1\neq 0.
}
\label{eq:odd_reading_nonzero_overlap}
\end{equation}

\section{Why the current explicit witness branch cannot activate the odd channel}

The explicit pure-even witness branch fixes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_\star=T^1,
\qquad
\gamma_E=1,
\qquad
\gamma_O=0.
}
\label{eq:odd_reading_pureE}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O=0,
\qquad
\beta=0.
}
\label{eq:odd_reading_pureE_zero}
\end{equation}

So the present explicit pure-even witness branch can never be used to read the odd coefficient.

\section{Immediate next branch decision}

To activate the odd channel, one must move from the pure-even witness branch to a mixed transverse branch with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\gamma_O\neq 0.
}
\end{equation}

Then the odd coefficient becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1\,I_{\theta,\cos},
}
\end{equation}
or, in the transport-side canonical notation,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_{\theta,\cos}.
}
\end{equation}

Thus the odd-channel problem is no longer structural.
It is now reduced to choosing the mixed branch and fixing the sign of \(\gamma_O\) relative to \(\beta_X\) and the overlap orientation.

\section{Final summary}

The explicit extra odd carrier route is already sufficient to read the odd coefficient.

Its reduced coefficient is
\[
\boxed{
\beta=I_{\theta,\cos}\widetilde\Lambda_O.
}
\]

At operator level,
\[
\boxed{
\widetilde\Lambda_O
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,C_OJ_1,
}
\]
so, in canonical explicit normalization,
\[
\boxed{
\beta
=
-\frac{\beta_X\gamma_O}{M_X^2}\,I_{\theta,\cos}
}
\]
up to the bookkeeping convention for \(J_1\).

Therefore the current pure-even explicit witness branch with \(\gamma_O=0\) necessarily has
\[
\boxed{
\beta=0.
}
\]

To proceed, the next branch must satisfy
\[
\boxed{
\gamma_O\neq 0.
}
\]

\section{Immediate Upgrade to the Mixed Transverse Branch}

\section{Short explanation}

The explicit pure-even canonical witness branch is no longer useful for the odd coefficient.
On that branch,
\[
\gamma_E=1,\qquad \gamma_O=0,
\]
so
\[
\beta=0
\]
is structurally forced. Therefore the next mathematically correct move is to leave the pure-even branch and move to the mixed transverse branch. 

\section{1. Mixed-branch master symbol}

The exact mixed-branch reduced symbol is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_1(p)
=
\frac12\,\alpha_X L_* I_{\theta'^3}\,p_\parallel\sigma_3
+
\beta_X I_\theta T_E\,(p_1\sigma_1+p_2\sigma_2)
+
\beta_X I_\theta T_O\,(-p_2\sigma_1+p_1\sigma_2).
}
\label{eq:mixed_master_symbol_now}
\end{equation}

Here
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*:=m_\parallel u_\parallel,
\qquad
T_*:=(T_E,T_O),
\qquad
R_\perp:=\sqrt{T_E^2+T_O^2}.
}
\label{eq:mixed_LT_now}
\end{equation}

The explicit overlap factors are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
I_\theta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{256}\theta_0^3\kappa^3.
}
\label{eq:mixed_overlaps_now}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:4]{index=4}

\section{2. Exact coefficient sheet on the mixed branch}

Therefore the exact reduced coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel
=
\frac12\,\alpha_XL_*I_{\theta'^3}
=
-\frac{3\sqrt3\pi}{512}\,\alpha_XL_*\,\theta_0^3\kappa^3,
}
\label{eq:mixed_lambda_now}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
\beta_XI_\theta T_E
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_XT_E\,\theta_0\kappa,
}
\label{eq:mixed_alpha_now}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\beta
=
\beta_XI_\theta T_O
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_XT_O\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:mixed_beta_now}
\end{equation}

Hence the exact nondegeneracy condition is simply
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_*\neq 0,
\qquad
R_\perp>0.
}
\label{eq:mixed_nondeg_now}
\end{equation}
Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_\parallel\neq 0,
\qquad
(\alpha,\beta)\neq(0,0).
}
\label{eq:mixed_nondeg_label_now}
\end{equation}
:contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\section{3. Polar transverse parametrization}

Write the transverse vector in polar form:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_E=R_\perp\cos\varphi,
\qquad
T_O=R_\perp\sin\varphi.
}
\label{eq:mixed_polar_now}
\end{equation}

Then
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\alpha
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_XR_\perp\cos\varphi\,\theta_0\kappa,
\qquad
\beta
=
-\frac{\sqrt3\pi}{16}\,\beta_XR_\perp\sin\varphi\,\theta_0\kappa.
}
\label{eq:mixed_polar_coeffs_now}
\end{equation}

So the odd/even ratio is exactly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\beta}{\alpha}=\tan\varphi
\qquad
(\cos\varphi\neq 0).
}
\label{eq:mixed_ratio_now}
\end{equation}

This is the cleanest branch-level reading of the odd coefficient:
\[
\varphi=0 \Longrightarrow \beta=0,
\qquad
\varphi\neq 0 \Longrightarrow \beta\neq 0
\]
provided \(\beta_X\theta_0\kappa R_\perp\neq0\).

\section{4. Canonical mixed sample}

So the longitudinal overlap remains order one while the transverse norm is enlarged by the \(\sqrt2\) factor. :contentReference[oaicite:6]{index=6}

\section{Branch-Consistent Mixed-Branch Same-Shell Support Criterion}

\section{Short explanation}

The pure-even same-shell benchmark is already fully reduced to the finite criterion
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
2a_K\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{EE}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1)},
\qquad
a_K=\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_pureeven_support}
\end{equation}
Its small-\(p\) drift is controlled by
\[
a_{+,i},\qquad a_{-,i},\qquad b_i,
\]
with
\[
a_{+,i}^{\mathrm{dir}}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right),
\qquad
a_{-,i}^{\mathrm{dir}}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right),
\qquad
b_i^{\mathrm{dir}}=0.
\]


The mixed transverse branch has
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_E=R_\perp\cos\varphi,
\qquad
T_O=R_\perp\sin\varphi,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt{T_E^2+T_O^2}.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_polar}
\end{equation}
In the canonical mixed sample,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4}.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_canonical}
\end{equation}


\section{1. Minimal branch-consistent uplift of the same-shell residual strength}

The pure-even same-shell correction strength is
\[
a_K=\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(\Lambda_E^{(0)})^2.
\]
For the mixed branch, the minimal branch-consistent uplift is to replace the single pure-even transverse amplitude by the full transverse norm:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_T
:=
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}R_\perp^2
=
\frac{\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}(T_E^2+T_O^2).
}
\label{eq:mixlift_aT}
\end{equation}

In the canonical mixed sample,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_T
=
\frac{2\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_aTcanonical}
\end{equation}

This is the smallest natural mixed-branch uplift of the pure-even \(KK\)-driven same-shell correction scale.

\section{2. Mixed transverse same-shell overlap package}

The pure-even support theorem is written in terms of the \(EE\)-overlap family
\[
\mathcal S_{++}^{EE}(p),\qquad
\mathcal S_{--}^{EE}(p),\qquad
\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}(p).
\]

On the mixed branch, the branch-consistent transverse overlap package is the quadratic form along the mixed direction
\[
T_*=(T_E,T_O).
\]
Define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{TT}(p;\varphi)
:=
\cos^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\sin^2\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
2\sin\varphi\cos\varphi\,\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p),
}
\label{eq:mixlift_STT}
\end{equation}
where \(a,b\in\{+,-\}\).

This is the minimal branch-consistent transverse same-shell overlap obtained by projecting the transverse correction sector along the activated mixed branch direction.

For the canonical mixed sample \(\varphi=\pi/4\),
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{ab}^{(\pi/4)}(p)
=
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{EE}(p)
+
\frac12\mathcal S_{ab}^{OO}(p)
+
\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}(p).
}
\label{eq:mixlift_Spi4}
\end{equation}

Likewise define the diagonal benchmark quantity
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
:=
\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(0)
=
\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(0)
}
\label{eq:mixlift_SdiagTT}
\end{equation}
whenever the valley-symmetric diagonal subcase holds.

\section{3. Mixed-branch same-shell block}

The pure-even same-shell block was
\[
H_{\mathrm{non\text{-}enr}}^{(1)}(p)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
d_+(p)&m(p)\\
\overline{m(p)}&d_-(p)
\end{pmatrix},
\]
with
\[
d_\pm(p)=E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(\pm p)-a_K\mathcal S_{\pm\pm}^{EE}(p),
\qquad
m(p)=B_{z_0}(p)-a_K\mathcal S_{+-}^{EE}(p).
\]

The branch-consistent mixed uplift is therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_+^{(T)}(p)
=
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(p)-a_T\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(p),
}
\label{eq:mixlift_dp}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
d_-^{(T)}(p)
=
E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(-p)-a_T\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(p),
}
\label{eq:mixlift_dm}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
m^{(T)}(p)
=
B_{z_0}(p)-a_T\mathcal S_{+-}^{TT}(p).
}
\label{eq:mixlift_mp}
\end{equation}

So the mixed-branch same-shell benchmark remains a \(2\times2\) Hermitian problem, but with the \(EE\)-overlap family replaced by the mixed \(TT\)-overlap family.

\section{4. Mixed-branch small-\(p\) drift coefficients}

Differentiate at \(p=0\). The direct core piece is unchanged:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{+,i}^{\mathrm{dir}}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right),
\qquad
a_{-,i}^{\mathrm{dir}}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right),
\qquad
b_i^{\mathrm{dir}}=0.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_directdrift}
\end{equation}

Now define the mixed derivative budgets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{+,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{++}^{TT}(p;\varphi)\right|_{p=0},
\qquad
\ell_{-,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{--}^{TT}(p;\varphi)\right|_{p=0},
}
\label{eq:mixlift_ellpm}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\ell_{0,i}^{TT}
:=
\left.\partial_{p_i}\mathcal S_{+-}^{TT}(p;\varphi)\right|_{p=0}.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_ell0}
\end{equation}

Then the full mixed-branch drift coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{+,i}^{(T)}
=
\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_T\ell_{+,i}^{TT},
}
\label{eq:mixlift_aplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
a_{-,i}^{(T)}
=
-\delta_{i\parallel}q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)
-
a_T\ell_{-,i}^{TT},
}
\label{eq:mixlift_aminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
b_i^{(T)}
=
-a_T\ell_{0,i}^{TT}.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_b}
\end{equation}

Define the norm-level budgets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
L_+^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{+,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_-^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{-,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2},
\qquad
L_0^{TT}
=
\Bigl(\sum_i|\ell_{0,i}^{TT}|^2\Bigr)^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_Lpm0}
\end{equation}

Thus
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_+^{(T)}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_+^{TT},
}
\label{eq:mixlift_Aplus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
A_-^{(T)}
\le
\left|q_*\!\left(Z-\frac{Yq_*^2}{2}\right)\right|
+
a_TL_-^{TT},
}
\label{eq:mixlift_Aminus}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
B^{(T)}
\le a_TL_0^{TT}.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_B}
\end{equation}

\section{5. Mixed-branch same-shell support criterion}

Exactly parallel to the pure-even case, define
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}
\le
\Bigl[
(\rho A_+^{(T)}+C_+^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
(\rho A_-^{(T)}+C_-^{TT}\rho^2)^2
+
2(\rho B^{(T)}+C_m^{TT}\rho^2)^2
\Bigr]^{1/2}.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_eps}
\end{equation}

Then a branch-consistent mixed same-shell sufficient condition is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|E_{z_0}^{\mathrm{dir}}(0)|-|B_{z_0}(0)|
>
2a_T\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_support}
\end{equation}

In the minimal scalar-only locked core,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
>
2a_T\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{TT}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,T)}.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_support_scalar}
\end{equation}

\section{6. Canonical mixed sample}

For
\[
T_E=T_O=1,
\qquad
R_\perp=\sqrt2,
\qquad
\varphi=\frac{\pi}{4},
\]
we have

and

+\mathcal S_{ab}^{EO}.

Therefore the canonical mixed same-shell sufficient condition becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{

\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.
}
\label{eq:mixlift_support_pi4}
\end{equation}

Equivalently, in scalar-only locked-core form,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\left|
-\mu^2+\frac{Zq_*^2}{4}-\frac{Yq_*^4}{16}+12uA^2
\right|
-
4uA^2
>
\frac{4\beta_X^2}{M_X^2}\,
\mathcal S_{\mathrm{diag}}^{(\pi/4)}
+
\varepsilon_{\mathrm{small}\text{-}p,\rho}^{(1,\pi/4)}.

\label{eq:mixlift_support_pi4_scalar}
\end{equation}

The mixed-branch coefficient sheet is exact. :contentReference[oaicite:5]{index=5}

\section{Corrected Residual Quartic Closure on the Exact Four-Class Shell Kernel}

\section{Current stage}

The project has reached the corrected residual quartic closure stage.
The carrier-side working-branch admissibility is already effectively closed, while the actual remaining frontier is the enlarged quartic residual kernel closure. The operational backend and the corrected seed are frozen as
\begin{equation}

(\mu^2,\lambda,\gamma)=(0.26,-0.43,1.62),
\qquad
\delta^{\mathrm{final}}=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096).

The correct reduced object is the projected residual map

=

not a naive reduced free-energy critical point.

\begin{equation}

and the quartic class averages

The simple compressed quartic shell kernel \((u,v,\kappa)\) fails strongly, with exact consistency defect

\Delta_{\rm ker}=32976.132300215555.

Hence the next exact reduced object must be built on the four-class shell kernel rather than the failed three-parameter compression.

\section{Four-class exact shell kernel}

The minimal enlarged quartic shell kernel is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_{\alpha\beta}^{(4c)}
=
u_d\,P^{(d)}_{\alpha\beta}
+
u_{\rm opp}\,P^{(\rm opp)}_{\alpha\beta}
+
u_\perp\,P^{(\perp)}_{\alpha\beta}
+
u_{\rm obl}\,P^{(\rm obl)}_{\alpha\beta},
}
\end{equation}
and at the corrected branch one identifies directly
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
u_d=U_d,\qquad
u_{\rm opp}=U_{\rm opp},\qquad
u_\perp=U_\perp,\qquad
u_{\rm obl}=U_{\rm obl}.
}
\end{equation}

After orbit reduction to the coarse \((A,E,O)\) basis, the exact four-class quartic reduced matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{(4c)}=
\begin{pmatrix}
\frac{U_d+U_{\rm opp}}{2} & U_\perp & U_{\rm obl}\\[1mm]
U_\perp & \frac{U_d+U_{\rm opp}}{2} & U_{\rm obl}\\[1mm]
U_{\rm obl} & U_{\rm obl} & \frac{U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+4U_{\rm obl}}{8}
\end{pmatrix}.

\label{eq:M4c_general}
\end{equation}

Substituting the corrected projected quartic data gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{(4c)}=
\begin{pmatrix}
8683.640035688459 & 9027.17290917827 & 2244.8894311890813\\

2244.8894311890813 & 2244.8894311890813 & 5550.147951811223
\end{pmatrix}.

\label{eq:M4c_numeric}
\end{equation}

\section{Quartic residual baseline at the corrected seed}

Write
\[
(a,e,o)=(\delta_A,\delta_E,\delta_O),
\qquad
r_A=a^2,\quad r_E=e^2,\quad r_O=o^2.

The quartic reduced residual contribution is
\begin{equation}

\qquad
X\in\{A,E,O\},

\end{equation}
where \(a_A=a\), \(a_E=e\), \(a_O=o\).

At the corrected seed
\[
(a,e,o)=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096),

r_A=r_O=(0.0096)^2=9.216\times10^{-5},

=

(a,e,o)=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096),

the corresponding quartic baseline is
\[
Q_A=8.494671573456258,\qquad
Q_E=8.241391656489691,\qquad
Q_O=2.580391735022780,
\]
and hence
\[
\boxed{
G^{(4)}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0.08154884710518008\\
-0.23735207970690309\\
0.024771760656218685
\end{pmatrix},
\qquad
\|G^{(4)}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})\|
=
0.25219013527770096.
}
\]

Since the actual corrected residual norm is
\[
\|G(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})\|\approx 0.03791852545979427,
\]
the nonquartic mismatch is necessarily large:
\[
\boxed{
\|G(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})-G^{(4)}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})\|
\ge
0.2142716098179067.
}
\]

Therefore the corrected local branch requires a large nonquartic completion beyond the exact four-class quartic baseline.

The first reduced target for the microscopic completion is the minimal diagonal quadratic completion
\[
G_X^{\rm model}
=
a_X\Bigl(q_X+\sum_Y M^{(4c)}_{XY}r_Y\Bigr),
\]
which forces
\[
\boxed{
q_A^\*=-8.494671573456258,\qquad
q_E^\*=-8.241391656489691,\qquad
q_O^\*=-2.580391735022780.
}
\]

The extracted orbit means
\[
\sigma_A=-115.81015796064617,\quad
\sigma_E=-105.83201242243113,\quad
\sigma_O=-108.719022860933
\]
cannot be identified directly with these targets, so the \(\sigma\)-sheet must still be interpreted only as an effective residual-based reduced sheet of the current solver family.

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Mainline result: the four-class quartic baseline is now fixed numerically, and the next microscopic task is to reproduce }
(q_A^\*,q_E^\*,q_O^\*)
}
\end{equation}
from the actual microscopic completion sources.

+

2244.8894311890813 & 2244.8894311890813 & 5550.147951811223
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Coarse \((A,E,O)\) quartic matrix}

\begin{pmatrix}

\end{pmatrix}.

\section{First numerical stability check of the enlarged quartic matrix}

The trace and determinant are
\begin{equation}
\Tr M^{(4c)} \approx 22917.428023188142,
\qquad
\det M^{(4c)} \approx -3.0305980590\times 10^{10}.
\end{equation}
Since the determinant is negative, the matrix is not positive definite.

Numerically, its eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_1\approx -343.533,\qquad
\lambda_2\approx 4771.217,\qquad
\lambda_3\approx 18489.744.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the enlarged four-class quartic kernel solves the basis problem,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{it is not itself a simple positive quartic free-energy closure on the corrected branch.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Quartic baseline at the corrected seed}

\section{Naive quartic stationary equations still fail}

If one nevertheless tries to build a quartic free-energy-like stationary system using the corrected linear orbit means,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma + M^{(4c)} r = 0,
\qquad
r=(r_A,r_E,r_O)^T,
\qquad
\sigma=(\sigma_A,\sigma_E,\sigma_O)^T,
}
\label{eq:naive_stationary}
\end{equation}
then solving \eqref{eq:naive_stationary} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_A^{\rm crit}\approx -1.031725\times 10^{-2},\qquad
r_E^{\rm crit}\approx 1.872843\times 10^{-2},\qquad
r_O^{\rm crit}\approx 1.618639\times 10^{-2}.
}
\label{eq:naive_stationary_solution}
\end{equation}

This candidate is immediately inadmissible because
\[
r_A^{\rm crit}<0.
\]

So the enlarged quartic basis does not restore a viable free-energy stationary interpretation.

\section{Mainline conclusion}

The exact four-class enlargement has now accomplished precisely one thing:
it removes the false \((u,v,\kappa)\) compression and provides the correct enlarged quartic shell basis.

But after this enlargement, the actual obstruction remains:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the correct next reduced object is the projected residual system }
G_A(\delta)=0,\quad G_E(\delta)=0,\quad G_O(\delta)=0,
}
\end{equation}
not a quartic free-energy stationary system.

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the basis problem is solved, but the residual-closure problem remains.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{3. Quartic residual Jacobian at the corrected seed}

For the quartic residual model
\[
G_X^{(4)}(a,e,o)
=
a_X\sum_Y M^{(4c)}_{XY}r_Y,
\qquad
r_Y=a_Y^2,
\]
the Jacobian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\bigl(J_{\rm res}^{(4c)}\bigr)_{ij}
=
\delta_{ij}Q_i
+
2a_i\,M^{(4c)}_{ij}\,a_j.
}
\label{eq:Jres_general}
\end{equation}

At the corrected seed this becomes
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\rm res}^{(4c)}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})
=
\begin{pmatrix}
10.095240102467715 & -4.991665531859216 & 0.4137780199567714\\
-4.991665531859216 & 22.646508448870943 & -1.2413340598703142\\
0.4137780199567714 & -1.2413340598703142 & 3.603395005929136
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Jres_numeric}
\end{equation}

Its eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_1(J_{\rm res}^{(4c)})\approx 3.52129589,\qquad
\lambda_2(J_{\rm res}^{(4c)})\approx 8.35219818,\qquad
\lambda_3(J_{\rm res}^{(4c)})\approx 24.47164948.
}
\label{eq:Jres_eigs}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\rm res}^{(4c)}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})\ \text{is positive definite.}
}
\end{equation}

This is the crucial actual result:
although the quartic matrix \(M^{(4c)}\) is indefinite as a free-energy object, the quartic residual map itself is locally well-conditioned at the corrected seed.

\section{4. Minimal diagonal quadratic completion target}

If one introduces the minimal diagonal quadratic completion

\end{equation}

+

\begin{pmatrix}
0.0055310 & 0.0055542 & 0.0032242\\
0.0055542 & 0.0052164 & 0.0028916\\
0.0032242 & 0.0028916 & 0.0124317
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:local_J_actual}
\end{equation}

Moreover the unconstrained Newton correction is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta_{\rm Newton}
\approx
(0.373633,\,-2.133560,\,-2.068666),
}
\end{equation}
which is effective at reducing the reduced residual norm but destroys the full BCC branch geometry. Therefore Newton-type descent is not the correct geometry-preserving solver. This is already established in the notes.

\section{Linearized action of the Jacobian on the corrected direction}

Now evaluate the current frozen corrected local seed in the local linear geometry:
\[
\delta^{\mathrm{final}}=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096)^T.
\]

Using \eqref{eq:local_J_actual}, one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J\,\delta^{\mathrm{final}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
-7.591104\times 10^{-5}\\
-6.915264\times 10^{-5}\\
\phantom{-}6.701856\times 10^{-5}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Jdelta_actual}
\end{equation}

Its norm is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|J\delta^{\mathrm{final}}\|
\approx
1.2267\times 10^{-4}.
}
\label{eq:Jdelta_norm_actual}
\end{equation}

Thus the linearized residual prediction at the corrected seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_{\rm lin}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})
=
G(0)+J\delta^{\mathrm{final}}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0.01637759\\
0.01496685\\
0.03074882
\end{pmatrix},
}
\end{equation}
with norm
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|G_{\rm lin}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})\|
\approx
0.03791730.
}
\label{eq:Glin_norm_actual}
\end{equation}

Compared with
\[
\|G(0)\|\approx 0.037923,
\]
this means that the frozen corrected direction produces only a tiny first-order residual change inside the local reduced geometry.

\section{Soft-mode structure of the reduced residual Jacobian}

The eigenvalues of \(J\) are approximately
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_1\approx -1.8549\times 10^{-4},\qquad
\lambda_2\approx 7.2905\times 10^{-3},\qquad
\lambda_3\approx 1.6074\times 10^{-2}.
}
\label{eq:J_eigs_actual}
\end{equation}

So the reduced residual Jacobian is nearly singular, with one very small soft (slightly unstable) mode.

Let \(v_{\rm soft}\) be the normalized eigenvector associated with \(\lambda_1\). Numerically,
\[
v_{\rm soft}\approx (0.7014,\,-0.7126,\,-0.0159).
\]

Normalize the corrected direction:
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\hat\delta
=
\frac{\delta^{\mathrm{final}}}{\|\delta^{\mathrm{final}}\|}.
}
\end{equation}
Then the overlap with the soft mode is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
|\hat\delta\cdot v_{\rm soft}|
\approx
0.8513.
}
\label{eq:soft_overlap_actual}
\end{equation}

Therefore the corrected geometry-preserving direction is strongly aligned with the near-null soft mode of the current reduced residual geometry.

\section{Mainline interpretation}

This computation explains the present stall in a precise way.

The issue is not that the corrected residual program lacks a reduced object.
It already has one:
\[
G_A(\delta)=0,\qquad G_E(\delta)=0,\qquad G_O(\delta)=0.
\]

The issue is also not that the current admissible correction direction is random.
Rather, the frozen corrected direction lies almost along the soft mode of the local Jacobian.

Hence:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the current admissible correction direction is almost first-order invisible to the reduced residual map.}
}
\end{equation}

So a first-order local Jacobian correction is not enough to close the branch.
This means that the next mainline step must genuinely go beyond the present local linear geometry.

\section{Correct next step}

Since the notes already state that the quartic basis must be enlarged from the failed \((u,v,\kappa)\) truncation to the four-class exact shell kernel, and that the corrected branch projection must be rerun on that enlarged basis, the present computation shows why this is unavoidable:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the local first-order reduced residual geometry is nearly flat along the corrected direction,}
}
\end{equation}
so
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{one must move to the enlarged four-class residual rerun and/or second-order non-diagonal completion.}
}
\end{equation}

This is the actual mainline consequence of the currently available branch data.

\section{Corrected Four-Class Orbit Equations and the Failure of the Free-Energy Stationary Route}

\section{Current stage}

The current stage is the corrected residual quartic closure stage.
The carrier-side working branch is already effectively closed, and the remaining obstruction is the quartic reduced-kernel closure on the corrected branch.
The frozen corrected seed and corrected projected coefficients are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^{\mathrm{final}}=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096),
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_A=-115.81015796064617,\qquad
\sigma_E=-105.83201242243113,\qquad
\sigma_O=-108.719022860933,
}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d=2493.1087739398513,\quad
U_{\rm opp}=14874.171297437068,\quad
U_\perp=9027.17290917827,\quad
U_{\rm obl}=2244.8894311890813.
}
\end{equation}

The exact orbit free-energy equations in the four-class basis are already given in closed form.
Under the \((A,E,O)\) orbit ansatz, the exact stationary system is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_A
=
(U_d+U_{\rm opp})r_A
+
2U_\perp r_E
+
8U_{\rm obl}r_O,
}
\label{eq:statA_corrected}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_E
=
2U_\perp r_A
+
(U_d+U_{\rm opp})r_E
+
8U_{\rm obl}r_O,
}
\label{eq:statE_corrected}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\sigma_O
=
2U_{\rm obl}(r_A+r_E)
+
(U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+4U_{\rm obl})r_O.
}
\label{eq:statO_corrected}
\end{equation}

So the corrected four-class free-energy reconstruction problem reduces exactly to the linear system
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{\rm stat}^{(4c)}
\begin{pmatrix}
r_A\\ r_E\\ r_O
\end{pmatrix}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\sigma_A\\ \sigma_E\\ \sigma_O
\end{pmatrix},
}
\end{equation}
with
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{\rm stat}^{(4c)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
U_d+U_{\rm opp} & 2U_\perp & 8U_{\rm obl}\\
2U_\perp & U_d+U_{\rm opp} & 8U_{\rm obl}\\
2U_{\rm obl} & 2U_{\rm obl} & U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+4U_{\rm obl}
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Mstat_general}
\end{equation}

\section{Numerical insertion of the corrected data}

Substituting the corrected projected quartic class means gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M_{\rm stat}^{(4c)}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
17367.28007137692 & 18054.34581835654 & 17959.11544951265\\
18054.34581835654 & 17367.28007137692 & 17959.11544951265\\
4489.778862378163 & 4489.778862378163 & 47600.68135400748
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Mstat_numeric}
\end{equation}

Its determinant is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\det M_{\rm stat}^{(4c)}
\approx
-9.697913788948185\times 10^{11},
}
\end{equation}
and its eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_1\approx -687.06574698,\qquad
\lambda_2\approx 32134.87964772,\qquad
\lambda_3\approx 47687.92985650.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the corrected four-class stationary matrix is itself indefinite.

\section{Closed-form reduction by sum and difference}

Define
\[
S:=r_A+r_E,\qquad
\Delta_r:=r_A-r_E.
\]
Subtracting \eqref{eq:statE_corrected} from \eqref{eq:statA_corrected} gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_r
=
\frac{\sigma_A-\sigma_E}{U_d+U_{\rm opp}-2U_\perp}.
}
\label{eq:Delta_r_corrected}
\end{equation}

Using the corrected data,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\Delta_r
=
\frac{-115.81015796064617+105.83201242243113}
{2493.1087739398513+14874.171297437068-2(9027.17290917827)}
\approx
0.01452283945470934.
}
\end{equation}

Adding \eqref{eq:statA_corrected} and \eqref{eq:statE_corrected}, one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
(U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp)S+16U_{\rm obl}r_O=\sigma_A+\sigma_E.
}
\label{eq:S_eq_corrected}
\end{equation}
Together with \eqref{eq:statO_corrected}, this yields the \(2\times2\) system
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\begin{pmatrix}
U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp & 16U_{\rm obl}\\
2U_{\rm obl} & U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+4U_{\rm obl}
\end{pmatrix}
\begin{pmatrix}
S\\ r_O
\end{pmatrix}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
\sigma_A+\sigma_E\\ \sigma_O
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

Numerically this gives
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S\approx -0.004205590866673833,
\qquad
r_O\approx -0.0020232985378032353.
}
\end{equation}

Finally
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_A=\frac{S+\Delta_r}{2}\approx 0.005158624294017749,
\qquad
r_E=\frac{S-\Delta_r}{2}\approx -0.009364215160691582.
}
\label{eq:rA_rE_corrected}
\end{equation}

So the corrected four-class algebraic critical point is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_A^{\rm crit}\approx 5.158624294017749\times 10^{-3},
\qquad
r_E^{\rm crit}\approx -9.364215160691582\times 10^{-3},
\qquad
r_O^{\rm crit}\approx -2.0232985378032353\times 10^{-3}.
}
\label{eq:rcrit_corrected}
\end{equation}

\section{Physical verdict}

The corrected four-class stationary point is still physically inadmissible because
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
r_E^{\rm crit}<0,
\qquad
r_O^{\rm crit}<0.
}
\end{equation}

Therefore:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{the four-class exact shell kernel solves the basis problem,}
}
\end{equation}
but
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{it does not rescue the reduced free-energy stationary picture on the corrected branch.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Mainline conclusion}

This is now the corrected analogue of the earlier unphysical free-energy critical point:
even after replacing the failed \((u,v,\kappa)\) truncation by the exact four-class shell kernel, the free-energy stationary route remains inadmissible.

Hence the next mathematically correct reduced object is not
\[
\partial_{r_I}\mathcal F_{\rm orb}=0,
\]
but the projected residual system
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G_A(r_A,r_E,r_O)=0,\qquad
G_E(r_A,r_E,r_O)=0,\qquad
G_O(r_A,r_E,r_O)=0.
}
\label{eq:correct_reduced_stationary_system_corrected}
\end{equation}

So the actual frontier is now sharply fixed:

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{not branch search, not quartic-basis truncation, but the direct residual-level orbit reduction.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Final summary}

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Current stage: corrected four-class quartic closure test on the frozen corrected branch.}
}
\end{equation}

Using the corrected projected data
\[
\sigma_A=-115.81015796064617,\quad
\sigma_E=-105.83201242243113,\quad
\sigma_O=-108.719022860933,
\]
\[
U_d=2493.1087739398513,\quad
U_{\rm opp}=14874.171297437068,\quad
U_\perp=9027.17290917827,\quad
U_{\rm obl}=2244.8894311890813,
\]
the exact four-class orbit stationary system is
\[
\sigma_A=(U_d+U_{\rm opp})r_A+2U_\perp r_E+8U_{\rm obl}r_O,
\]
\[
\sigma_E=2U_\perp r_A+(U_d+U_{\rm opp})r_E+8U_{\rm obl}r_O,
\]
\[
\sigma_O=2U_{\rm obl}(r_A+r_E)+(U_d+U_{\rm opp}+2U_\perp+4U_{\rm obl})r_O.
\]

Its corrected algebraic critical point is
\[
\boxed{
r_A^{\rm crit}\approx 5.158624294017749\times 10^{-3},
\qquad
r_E^{\rm crit}\approx -9.364215160691582\times 10^{-3},
\qquad
r_O^{\rm crit}\approx -2.0232985378032353\times 10^{-3}.
}
\]

Therefore the corrected four-class free-energy stationary point is still physically inadmissible:
\[
\boxed{
r_E^{\rm crit}<0,
\qquad
r_O^{\rm crit}<0.
}
\]

So the exact four-class shell kernel solves the quartic basis problem, but it does not rescue the free-energy stationary picture on the corrected branch.

\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\text{Mainline result: the next reduced object must be the projected residual system }G_A=G_E=G_O=0.
}
\end{equation}
