\section{First Genuine Non-Diagonal Residual Completion at the Corrected Branch}

\section{Current stage}

The current project stage is the corrected residual quartic closure stage.
The carrier-side working branch is already effectively closed, while the actual remaining frontier is the enlarged quartic residual closure.
The correct reduced object is the projected residual map
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G(\delta)
=
\begin{pmatrix}
G_A(\delta)\\
G_E(\delta)\\
G_O(\delta)
\end{pmatrix},
}
\end{equation}
with frozen corrected seed
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\delta^{\mathrm{final}}=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096).
}
\end{equation}

The corrected projected quartic class data are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
U_d=2493.1087739398513,\quad
U_{\rm opp}=14874.171297437068,\quad
U_\perp=9027.17290917827,\quad
U_{\rm obl}=2244.8894311890813.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Exact four-class quartic baseline}

The coarse \((A,E,O)\) four-class quartic reduced matrix is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
M^{(4c)}=
\begin{pmatrix}
8683.640035688459 & 9027.17290917827 & 2244.8894311890813\\
9027.17290917827 & 8683.640035688459 & 2244.8894311890813\\
2244.8894311890813 & 2244.8894311890813 & 5550.147951811223
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\end{equation}

At the corrected seed
\[
(a,e,o)=(0.0096,-0.0288,0.0096),
\]
one gets
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
Q=
\begin{pmatrix}
8.494671573456258\\
8.241391656489691\\
2.580391735022780
\end{pmatrix},
}
\end{equation}
hence
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G^{(4)}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})
=
\begin{pmatrix}
0.08154884710518008\\
-0.23735207970690309\\
0.024771760656218685
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:G4_corr}
\end{equation}

The quartic residual Jacobian at the corrected seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\rm res}^{(4c)}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})
=
\begin{pmatrix}
10.095240102467715 & -4.991665531859216 & 0.4137780199567714\\
-4.991665531859216 & 22.646508448870943 & -1.2413340598703142\\
0.4137780199567714 & -1.2413340598703142 & 3.603395005929136
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:J4_corr}
\end{equation}

\section{Residual-side local completion problem}

We now seek a local residual model of the form
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G^{\rm model}(\delta)=S\delta+G^{(4)}(\delta),
}
\end{equation}
where \(S\) is a constant \(3\times 3\) completion matrix.

To make the corrected seed an exact stationary point of this local model, one must impose
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
G^{\rm model}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})=0
\quad\Longleftrightarrow\quad
S\,\delta^{\mathrm{final}}=-G^{(4)}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}}).
}
\label{eq:completion_constraint}
\end{equation}

This is the first residual-side completion problem beyond the failed free-energy reconstruction route.

\section{Minimal symmetric completion}

We restrict to symmetric completions
\[
S=S^T,
\]
and ask for the minimum-Frobenius-norm solution of \eqref{eq:completion_constraint}.

Let
\[
d:=\delta^{\mathrm{final}},
\qquad
g:=G^{(4)}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}}),
\qquad
u:=\frac{d}{\|d\|},
\qquad
w:=\frac{-g}{\|d\|}.
\]
Then the unique minimum-Frobenius symmetric solution is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\min}
=
u w^T+w u^T-(u^Tw)\,uu^T.
}
\label{eq:Smin_formula}
\end{equation}

A direct substitution shows that \(S_{\min}=S_{\min}^T\) and
\[
S_{\min}d=-g.
\]

Numerically,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
S_{\min}=
\begin{pmatrix}
-0.839960218174805 & 2.450804313533534 & -0.302298414680853\\
2.450804313533534 & -7.145183917627953 & 0.837818903051675\\
-0.302298414680853 & 0.837818903051675 & 0.235363388813100
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Smin_numeric}
\end{equation}

Its Frobenius norm is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|S_{\min}\|_F\approx 8.087899329725037.
}
\end{equation}

\section{Comparison with the diagonal-only completion}

The diagonal-only completion that enforces stationarity is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
D^\*=\operatorname{diag}(-Q_A,-Q_E,-Q_O)
=
\operatorname{diag}(-8.494671573456258,\,-8.241391656489691,\,-2.580391735022780).
}
\label{eq:Dstar}
\end{equation}

Its Frobenius norm is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|D^\*\|_F\approx 12.113562774127091.
}
\end{equation}

So even before checking stability, the smallest symmetric completion is already genuinely non-diagonal and smaller in norm than the diagonal-only completion.

\section{Off-diagonal content is unavoidable}

Decompose
\[
S_{\min}=S_{\min}^{\rm diag}+S_{\min}^{\rm off}.
\]
Numerically,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\|S_{\min}^{\rm diag}\|_F\approx 7.198234666196914,
\qquad
\|S_{\min}^{\rm off}\|_F\approx 3.687754500794174.
}
\end{equation}

Hence the off-diagonal sector contributes the non-negligible fraction
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\frac{\|S_{\min}^{\rm off}\|_F}{\|S_{\min}\|_F}
\approx 0.4559594958409981.
}
\end{equation}

So the first corrected residual completion is not merely a tiny perturbative off-diagonal tweak.
Its off-diagonal part is order one relative to the whole completion.

\section{Local Jacobian after the symmetric completion}

The completed residual Jacobian at the corrected seed is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\rm tot}
=
J_{\rm res}^{(4c)}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})+S_{\min}.
}
\end{equation}

Numerically,
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\rm tot}
=
\begin{pmatrix}
9.255279884292909 & -2.540861218325682 & 0.111479605275918\\
-2.540861218325682 & 15.501324531242990 & -0.403515156818639\\
0.111479605275918 & -0.403515156818639 & 3.838758394742236
\end{pmatrix}.
}
\label{eq:Jtot_numeric}
\end{equation}

Its eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_1(J_{\rm tot})\approx 3.824699013629953,\qquad
\lambda_2(J_{\rm tot})\approx 8.352431280003644,\qquad
\lambda_3(J_{\rm tot})\approx 16.418232516644533.
}
\label{eq:Jtot_eigs}
\end{equation}

Therefore
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\rm tot}\ \text{is positive definite.}
}
\end{equation}

\section{Contrast with the diagonal-only completion}

If one instead uses the diagonal completion \(D^\*\), the completed Jacobian is
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
J_{\rm diag}=J_{\rm res}^{(4c)}(\delta^{\mathrm{final}})+D^\*.
}
\end{equation}
Its eigenvalues are
\begin{equation}
\boxed{
\lambda_1(J_{\rm diag})\approx -0.11554365,\qquad
\lambda_2(J_{\rm diag})\approx 0.91059735,\qquad
\lambda_3(J_{\rm diag})\approx 16.23363488.
}
\end{equation}

So the diagonal-only completion makes the corrected seed stationary, but still leaves a negative mode.
By contrast, the minimum-norm symmetric non-diagonal completion both enforces stationarity and restores positive local residual geometry.

\section{Mainline consequence}

This is the first genuine non-repetitive mainline result beyond the four-class quartic baseline:

\begin{enumerate}
\item the corrected branch cannot be closed by a diagonal-only completion;
\item the first viable local completion is genuinely non-diagonal;
\item the smallest symmetric completion already has a substantial off-diagonal sector;
\item once that non-diagonal completion is included, the corrected seed becomes both stationary and locally stable in the residual model.
\end{enumerate}

Therefore the next microscopic completion source must reproduce a matrix of the same qualitative type as \(S_{\min}\), not merely the diagonal target \(q^\*\).

Equivalently,
\begin{equation}

}
\end{equation}

\section{Final summary}
